After I completed for you, oh sons, this book, which is the last of the science in medicine with its complement, and I reached the end of it, from its explanations and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since the operation with the hand has been neglected in our region and in our time it has been entirely abandoned; until perhaps its science has perished and its track has been cut off; and there have not remained of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands have altered; and error and hesitation occurred to them, until its intentions were closed and its use was prolonged. It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise concerning it, according to the method of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and that I should come with the forms of iron instruments of cauterization, and the rest of the instruments of the work; made from the addition of declarations and from the preparation of what is necessary.
The reason for which a good artisan of it with his hand is not found in our time, is: that the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to exercise beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen described, until he knows the instruments of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction, and separation, and has cognition of the bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their origin, and the pulsations of the veins, and the quiet ones, and the places of their exits.
And because of that, Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken about that in the introduction to this book.
Since he who is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy, does not understand, and already falls into error, by which men are harmed: just as I have seen many of them, who pretend to be knowledgeable about this science, and boast about it without knowledge, and without experience.
What happened was that the surgeon cut a stubborn tumor of the aposteme scrofula on the neck of a woman and cut some arteries on the neck so the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead at his hands.
And I saw another surgeon who presumed to extract a stone from a man which had grown during his lifetime and the stone was large. He therefore cut to it, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. So the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had already been called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the weakness of the man that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke of our land because of medicine, and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him that he got a fracture in his leg near the heel, and the doctor hastened with his ignorance and pressed the fracture above the wound with poultices and tight bandages and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he treated him according to his desires. Afterwards he left him for some days and ordered him not to undo the bandage, and it remained so until his leg became an aposteme and his foot, and it led to destruction.
I was therefore called to him, and I hastened to undo the bandage, and quietness followed, and he was relieved from his pains.
However the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb, and I could not restrain it.
Then the corruption ceased to spread through the limb until he died.
And I saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous aposteme and it became an ulcer after some days, until the evil of it became great with its master.
What is, that when it is a pure cancer from melancholic humor, then it is not suitable to be pierced with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can tolerate it, so that the whole of it can be cut off.
And for that reason, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation to which health is associated, and an operation in which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already stirred up in every place of this book, where the operation comes, in which there is terror and fear.
For it is necessary for you to beware of that and dismiss it, so that the foolish do not find a way to speak and to dishonor.
Receive therefore the measure with solicitude and protection, and your weak ones with facility and firmness, and use the better way leading by the grace of God to salvation and laudable succession: and dismiss terrible anxieties of difficult healing: and lift your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation enters into your faith and your commodity.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and elevated in this world, and afterwards to your quantities.
For Galen has already said in certain of his admonitions. Do not call the bad sickness medicine, nor name it evil doctor.
Now however I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
The first chapter.
Of cauterization with fire and of cauterization with sharp medicine, the chapter, and ordered from head to feet, and forms of instruments, and iron tools of cauterization: and all that is necessary in the operation.
The second chapter.
Of cutting and piercing, bloodletting and puncture, and of wounds: and the removal of arrows, and similar things to that: and the entire chapter, arranged in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter.
Of restoration, and dislocation, and the cure of twisting, and similar things to that: the chapter, arranged from head to foot, and in the forms of instruments.
But before I mention the operation with it, it is necessary that I say the quality of its cauterizations, and of its ulcers: and in what complexion they are exhibited.
I say therefore, that the discourse on the quality of cauterization and ulcer, is a discourse subtle and profound, of science and of hidden secret.
And many wise men have spoken on it, and have disagreed about it: and to me it is sufficient to take a little from their discourses, fearing prolixity.
I say therefore, that cauterization is suitable universally for every complexion, which is with matter, and without matter: excepting two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
In the hot and dry complexions with matter they disagree. For some have said that cauterization is suitable for it. And others have said the opposite of that, namely that cauterization is not suitable for the disease which is from heat and dryness: since the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable, that a hot and dry disease should be treated with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite of that says: that what is done by cauterization is a remedy for every hot and dry ailment that occurs in the bodies of men, because when you examine the body of a man and its humidities in relation to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a man to be cold.
And I indeed say through his speech: that the experiment has already revealed that to me many times.
But truly it is not fitting that he come upon that, unless he who has already been tested and practiced in the chapter of cauterization's last exercise, and knows the diversity of the complexions of men, and the disposition of ailments within themselves, and their causes and accidents, and the space of time of them.
From the remaining complexions, however, there is not above use fear: and especially in cold and moist ailments. For all physicians have already agreed on these, and they do not disagree regarding treatment with cauterization in them.
And know, my sons, that the secret of curing by cauterization with fire and its goodness over cauterization with burning medicine is: because fire is simple, whose action does not penetrate except to the member which is cauterized, and it does not harm another member joined to it, except with little harm.
The action of burning medicine, however, penetrates to that which extends from the members, and perhaps it causes an ailment difficult to cure to occur in a member, and perhaps it kills.
Fire, however, on account of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now indeed that has become known to us through experiment, on account of the length of service and study with art, and standing upon the truth of things: and because of that I will excuse the length of speech.
And if it were not, I would not be allowed to reveal to you in this my book a secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies through its expulsion, which expels diseases, demonstrated by philosophical speech, which will be sharpened in your minds.
And know, my sons, that they themselves disagree about the time in which it is suitable to perform a cauterization, and they put forth a better time in spring.
And I say that a cauterization is suitable at any time, because the harm that occurs on account of the time is outweighed by the benefit that is attracted with the cauterization. And especially if the cauterization is on account of pains from necessary pains, strong, urgent ones, which do not tolerate delay: because it is feared that a greater evil will occur from them, than the small harm that occurs on account of the time.
And let it not fall into your minds, O my sons, that which they do not consider, except the common and foolish physicians, namely that those diseases which are healed by a cauterization, do not always relapse: and they propose that consequence, and the thing is not as they think: because a cauterization is not, unless in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and evacuates the humidities which are the causes, why pains occur.
However, the cauterization surpasses medicine by the speed of its health, and the virtue of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible, that the disease may return at some hour of time according to the complexion of the infirm, and the location of its disease, and its virtue: and what is prepared in its body from an aggregation of superfluities in it: and what pervades into it in acquiring them from foods, and similar things from those causes, unless a disease is made, in which a cauterization is administered.
A subtle inflammation in a member causes little excess and moisture, such as a cauterization of the tooth, because of pain, and similar things to it, it is possible that the pain does not return to it. But that happens in few cases.
And I speak to the common people again, that cauterization is the last of medicine, is a straightforward speech: not according to what they themselves intend in it: since they believe that there is no cure which is conferred with medicine, nor with anything else after the application of the cauterization.
The thing is contrary to that, and the intention, that cauterization is the last of medicine, is not, except that when we administer modes of cure in some disease, and those medicines do not confer: then we administer at the end of the thing a cauterization, and it confers: then it falls, that cauterization is the last of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish doctors understand.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say that except because of the equality of gold, and the subtlety of its substance: and they said that it does not produce pus in the place of the cauterization. But it is not absolutely true: since I have already proven that and found that it does not do that in certain bodies without others.
And cauterization with gold is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you make cauterization fire from gold, it is not declared to you, when it is ignited according to the quantity that you use, because of the redness of gold: and when it approaches the cold, and if you add ignition on top of it, it melts in the fire, and turns into sheets.
Wherefore the craftsman falls from that in work: and because of that cauterization with iron is done by us more quickly and nearer to the rightness of operation.
And I have already arranged this chapter on cauterization, following the chapters, and I have arranged them from head to feet, so that they provide to the inquirer what he wants from it.
Head II.
This cauterization is useful for dominating humidity and chill on the brain: which two are causes of swelling, and an abundance of flowing humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and an abundance of sleep, and pain in the teeth, and pain in the throat: and universally all sickness that occurs from chill, such as palsy, and swelling, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar to those sicknesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should first prepare the weak person: so that they are evacuated in the beginning with a cleansing medicine for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the weak person demands, and their age, and their habit.
Then order them to shave their head with a razor. Then have them sit between your hands in a square shape, so that they now place their hands on their chest.
Then put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that place with an incision.
Then prepare the olive cautery for ignition, whose shape is this.
Then put it on the marked place with an incision, lowering it, as your hand is tightened little by little, and you rotate it. Then lift your hand quickly, and look at the place.
If you see that it has already taken from the bone a quantity of head alkali, or a quantity of zeherb, then lift your hand. And if not, then move your hand with the iron itself or with something else by means of it, if it becomes cold: until the bones which I mentioned to you are visible.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cotton in it, and put it on the place: and leave it for three days.
Then put on it cotton soaked in butter, and leave it on the place, until the eschar is destroyed by fire. Then treat it with the ointment tetrapharmacon, until it is healed.
Now they have said that the more a wound remains open, the more it emits pus, therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone: and that the cautery should be applied until something adheres to the thickness of the bone.
Then scrape after that which has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to penetrate with the cautery to the extreme, until it impresses on the bone an impression of a mold, so that the bone falls, which is made like the form of a crate: or the instrument that women put on by means of the alphabet infusion: and they extract, what they breathe out from this place vapors of the head, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then treat it, until it becomes consolidated.
To me, however, these two types of cautery do not seem suitable except in certain men according to the path of fear.
And to leave it alone is better for me with its own health.
For the head is weakened by the dissolution of its natural continuity: as we have been shown in the other members: and especially when the head is weak and feeble by nature: and a certain type of cautery is more salutary and better for me, and I approve it: therefore operate with it for health.
Chapter 3.
When there is a chronic pain in the whole head: and it is prolonged to the weak, and it is treated with henna, and quinine, and head purges, and oils, and plasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and none of those things help it: then consider. For if the head of the weak person is of strong natural creation, and it is not weak, and it has found intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery under that a little. Then cauterize it itself over every horn of its head with a cautery, so that the skin is not pierced, and a quantity is discovered from the bone, which we have described. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of its head, in the place which is called "uas": and it is a place where the ventose is put: and raise your target in this, and do not uncover the bone. For the weak person finds it due to that vehement pain, and different from the pain of the other cauterizations of the whole head.
And I will say that this Cautery in its own place: and it is necessary that it be a cautery, with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and its back is more subtly cauterized than the middle of the head.
Chapter 4.
When there is pain and swelling in one part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is treated with medicines that cleanse the head, and the rest of the treatment is administered, which I mentioned in the divisions of illnesses, and none of that helps: then cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with sharp burning medicine: or with iron.
Cauterization with acute burning medicine is such that you take one tooth of a badger, and scrape it, and cut off its extremities on both sides. Then cut the place of pain at the time with a broad lancet, until a place is made under the skin, in which the dens is captured.
Insert it then under the skin, until it is hidden: then bind over it with a poultice of decent constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours; then undo it, and extract the badger, and leave the wound two days, or three: afterwards put on it a plaster submerged in butter, until the place makes pus: then cure it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you want to make it with certain burning medicines, which I wrote in the twelfth treatise, on medicines for burning.
But cauterization of it with iron is according to this method. Fire cauterization, whose form is this.
And it is called a Clavulus: because the form of its head is like the form of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in the middle of it is a certain small prominence.
Then put it on the place, and hold your hand: and you withdraw the iron little by little with speed: and let the quantity that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, as its middle. And raise your hand, so that the artery which is beneath is not burned, and there occurs a flow of blood.
Then soak the plaster in salt water, and put it on the place, and leave it for three days: then put a plaster with butter: afterwards cure it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this half of the skull with the edge of a second cauterizing knife. And beware of cutting the arterial vein in this half of the skull, not being old is a particular property.
On the method of cauterizing in the old half skull.
When you treat the half skull, with what we said in the preceding treatment, and what we said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment is not effective: and you see from the disease that what we said about the first cauterization with medicine or with fire is not sufficient for it, then you must use a sharp cauterizing iron, until it becomes white after you make a sign above the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or something like that: and put your hand in its place, and press it until you cut the artery, and penetrate to the bone.
Truly it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jawbone, which moves during mastication, lest the side or nerve that moves it be scorched, whence spasms occur.
And this is above caution and warning about the flow of arterial blood which has been severed. For in cutting it off there is fear, and especially for him who does not know what he does, and is neither careful nor experienced: and he gives up the operation at the start.
And I come with a reminder of the treatment of the flow of blood that occurs from an artery, according to its own method, and in the proper place of this book.
What if you see from the disease that this cauterization is not sufficient for it, and you see the weak body tolerating a cauterization on the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cauterization that we spoke of in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cauterizing iron having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
On the method of cauterizing for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold and is treated with solutiuis and the rest of the treatment that we mentioned in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then cauterization by fire: and it is that which is called a punctum, whose shape is this.
Then prick it with that after its ignition all around the entire ear, as it revolves: or around both, if pain is in both. And extend yourself with the cautery from the root of the ear for a little while, after you have marked the place with ink: and let the quantity of the cautery be ten punctures on all the ear, or about that.
Then treat the places until they heal.
On the method of cauterizing for twisting.
Chapter Seven.
Twisting that is treated with cauterization is not except for the types which occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And it lacks cauterization of the type that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this type of twisting with hiers and purging of the head and gargling and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the weak place with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little below its temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And put your cauterization on the opposite side of the weak part. For softening does not occur except in the part that appears healthy.
And the shape of the cauterization is that you should cauterize it with a cauterity on the direct extremity of the upper ear under the horn of the head a little, and another in the temple: whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And put your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the Cautery, and it is a type from a knife, whose shape has been described above: nevertheless it is not thinner than that little, as you see: and it is necessary that the knife be a little above superfluous grossness.
Then treat the place with what has gone before until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in old Apoplexy.
When the Apoplexy becomes old and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication is not effective, and the weak person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cauterization on the back of the head, according to what has gone before: and the method of the cauterization should be according to what has gone before.
And he is also cauterized with a Cautery on the bone of the stomach: and it is even more extreme.
Then let him be treated with what has gone before.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that the weak person be given first a drink of great hiera, and purging pills to cleanse the brain.
Then shave the entire head of the weak person, and put on his back of the head a plaster made from mustard as described in the treatise on plasters: and apply it to him several times.
This indeed is the method of Cautery: and do that according to the same order which I mentioned there.
If therefore he is healed by it, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the back of his head, which extend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and put between each cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cauterization, with what has preceded.
If however you need to add and he is weak for bearing it: then perform the cauterization in the middle. What if you need to add: then cauterize it above the two horns.
Then treat it, until it is healed: and let the cauterization be applied according to the form which has been described.
On the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter 10.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with caution, and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the weak person: afterwards cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle of the head, and with a cauterization above each horn of the head, and with a cauterization above its back, and with three on the vertebrae of the neck.
If however you immerse in the disease of softening of the body more than those, and he is weak for bearing it, and the disease is strong: then cauterize it with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and lastly with a cauterization, until much of its skin is burned, and lift your hand. Then treat it, until it is healed: and thus the cauterization will be successful.
On the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized, unless it is he whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
It is necessary therefore that you cleanse his brain first with caution, and with the rest of the treatment which we have spoken of in the division: when he is greatly weak, or is bearing the reception of medicines.
If however he is a boy, who does not bear medicines, then let him be given a gargle and purging mastics which cleanse the brain, for many days before with improvement of foods.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cauterization in the middle of the head, according to what has preceded in manner: and cauterize another on his occiput, and all over each horn of his head with a cauterization. What if he is weak and strong, and will be tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauterizations that I mentioned in one having paralysis, and mollification of the body over the spondiles of the neck, and the spondiles of the back: and let the Cauterium be olive oil according to the method which has preceded.
If however he is a weak child, then put a subtle cauterization, according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humidities and gross phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauterizations that we mentioned in one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity inclined to melancholy, and the body of the weak person is humid, then give him in a drink what will cleanse his brain, according to what has preceded in division: afterwards shave the head of the weak person, and make then a tortella made from linen, as a circle.
Then put it on the middle of the head: and the weak person sitting squarely should be held from every side.
Then present an ointment. And it is worthy made from old butter of eggs. And warm it over a fire with a tempered measure of heat, which the finger can tolerate, when it is inserted into it. Then apply it on the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it becomes cool.
Do that to the weak person once a week, with the rest of his good regime, until he is cured.
Or use a cautery making many small points on it, besides which burn the hand with the cautery: apply it while smelling.
This type of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then put on it a cotton cloth soaked in butter or hen's fat.
Of the method of cauterizing with water descending to the eye.
Chapter 13.
When the origin of the water in the eye is declared to you by signs, which I mentioned in the division, then begin and apply a poultice to the weak part, with that which will cleanse its head.
And keep it away from all moistures, and make it sit in a bath, in fasting for some days.
Then order it to shave its head, and to cauterize itself in the middle of its head. Then cauterize it on the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a simultaneous flow of water in both eyes: or on one side, if there is a flow of water in one eye: and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in width across the temples: and cauterize to stop the flow of blood.
What if you see anything of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them, and caution against the flow of blood.
And when it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries ultimately brought forth.
Of the method of cauterizing for old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and frequent: and they are above the veins and arteries which are on the manifest outer head, it is verified that this is from cold and phlegmatic superfluities: then cauterize with the same cautery that I narrated in the descent of water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if you apply an addition, then cauterize it on every part with a cautious eye, above the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in the nasal polyp.
When you treat it with what we said in the division and the treatment is not effective then hasten and give a drink of weak cichorias for three nights then shave its head and cauterize it with a moderate cautery with an olive cautery. Then cauterize it with a cautery of the nape of the neck with two cauteries, above two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And beware of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the cautery of the nape of the neck.
On the method of cauterizing for softening the Eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by sickness or moisture then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every side and they will stretch out from both temples and let the length of each cautery be according to the lengths of the eyebrow and do not extend your hand with the cautery except according to the quantity that the third eyelid is burned.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when inverted eyelashes prick the eye.
The cautery in this is according to two methods: either a cautery with fire or a cautery with burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, instruct the weak one beforehand so that he let his eyelashes drop if he is one of those who clean them until they are prolonged and equal. If they sting him near his eyes: then constrict his eyes with a cloth, so that they do not move, until they heal.
When therefore the wounds heal and become equal, then put the head of the sick person in your lap: afterwards apply a mark above the eyelid of his eyes with a caustic, a mark which is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then put a cloth soaked in egg white on the eye, or a dressing of psyllium over the eye.
Then apply cautery with fire, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the figure that you marked little by little on many places, until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, entirely appearing properly.
And the sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contract, and the hairs rise up at the puncture of the eye.
Raise your hand therefore then: and leave it for three days.
Then put on it a cloth with butter, until the scar is eradicated. Then treat it with ointment, until it heals.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cauterization over that place, as you did at first.
If the hairs are on the underside: then cauterize it, until they rise up to their natural place: and become equal so that the hairs do not sting the eye.
It is to warn the sick person, that he let the hairs be, until they grow out and become even. Make from a paper of cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unimbibed lime a weight of one ounce or nearly that; then rub them together with good friction, and make that with speed, so that it does not become cold. Then take from the same a piece and place it on a paper which you made like a shape of myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid of one eye or two. And place under the eye a cotton imbued with egg white: and let the head of the weak person be in your lap.
And put your index finger on the medicine, and press it for a short while. And you move it as often as the weak person feels the biting of the medicine: since its biting is found like fire.
While therefore it continues to find the biting, then dismiss the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting has quieted, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid raised, as it is raised with contraction by fire, or with incision, it is good: and if not, then apply again on it from the medicine on the place, where the medicine does not imprint and does not denigrate, until your operation equals and the eye contracts.
Then put on it a cotton with butter, until the skin is eradicated of burning. Then treat it with ointment called diaphenicum, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation, to guard with utmost care, lest something from the medicine falls into the eye.
What if the eyelid becomes soft after some days, and something from the hair pushes into the eye, then apply again medicine on that place which becomes soft from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it, until it heals.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore your consideration should be according to that, and the path of rectitude will not be hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing in the tear duct.
When you treat the fistula, with what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Order the weak person to place their head on your lap, and let your assistant hold their head between their hands in such a way that it does not move or stir with their head.
Then put a small pad under the conjunctiva of the eye, or in the mucus of the eyelid above their eye: then apply the cauterization instrument, whose shape is this.
Let it be hollow, in the shape of a feather quill from one end, with which cauterization is made: and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it to be held thus.
However this hollow one is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract the sanies from it, and clean it: and if it is not open, then open it, and extract its pus.
Then put on it a cauterization iron, which is made very hot.
And hold your hand for a little while with the cauterization instrument near the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand does not tremble or disturb the weak person: and you put the cauterization instrument on the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If then you cauterize at the beginning up to the mouth, it will be good. And if not: then repeat the cauterization once or twice, if you consider it necessary: and diminish that for three days.
Then put a plaster with butter, and treat it with excitative ointment, until it is healed.
Which if it exceeds for him forty days, and it is not healed: then put on it a sharp corrosive medicine, until the mouth is laid bare: and shave it according to what is described in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the first authorities have described. Direct to the place of the fistula, and probe it: then put in the same fissure a thin tube, that is, a subtle cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it a quantity of a drachm of melted lead, and hold your hand with the cane in good retention, and do not move the weak one at all, so that it does not run or the melted lead reaches its eye.
And it is fitting to put on the weak eye a plaster under the white of the eye, or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a wonderful healing.
What if the fistula is healed, with what we have said about cauterization, and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come into its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing in the fissures of the lips.
Many times there occur in the lip fissures, which are called Pili, and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat their fissures, with what we have said in the division of ailments, and the treatment does not work, then apply a small cauterization to the scalpel, according to this method.
And let it be shaped according to the fineness of the scalpel.
Then put the ignited thing quickly into the same fissures, until the cauterization penetrates to the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a dressing, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in a fistula of the mouth.
When an apostema occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it makes pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes chronic and the pus flows and a fistula is formed: then you treat it and if the treatment does not work, then it is necessary to apply a cauterization according to the quantity that the fistula can contain. Then insert the ignited thing into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand, until the ignited iron penetrates to its depth and bottom: do that once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards, with what we have said about treatment, until it is cured.
If the pus is then cut off and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what appears at its head.
On the method of cauterizing in the gums and softened teeth.
When the gum becomes softened because of humidity, and the teeth are loose, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not work: then put the head of the weak one on your lap.
Then apply a cauterization, whose form will appear after this, so that you put a reed on the tooth: and insert into it the ignited cauterization quickly: and hold your hand for a little while, until the weak one feels the heat of the fire has already penetrated to the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cauterization several times, according to what you need.
Then let the weak bone fill itself with salty water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For a dense motion is strengthened, and the softened gum is constricted, and the corrupted humidity is dried.
On the method of cauterizing for toothache.
When the toothache is due to cold or there is cold or worms in it, and treatment with medicines is not effective: then cauterization of it is according to two methods: either cauterization with butter, or cauterization with fire.
But the cauterization of it with butter is, that you take cow's butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a pan. Then take the butter, and apply it to the end of the affected tooth. Then submerge it in the boiling butter: and place it quickly on the painful tooth, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the power of the fire penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you want, submerge a thread, or cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth: and put over it a heated iron, until the fire penetrates to the deep concavity of the tooth.
But the cauterization of it with fire is, that you heat a bronze or iron tube. And let there be in its body something of thickness, so that the sharpness of the fire does not penetrate to the weak tooth.
Then cauterize with fire, whose shape will come: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand, until the cauterization cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be relieved, either on that same day, or another day.
And it is necessary in the application of that cauterization, that it fill the weak bone with good pus, and that it hold it for one hour; then it expels it.
And this is the form of the cauterization.
Cauterize with a cauterizing iron whichever extremity you use, according to what is possible: and this is the form of the Cannula.
Of the method of cauterizing in Strophules.
When Strophules are from phlegm and from cold humidities, and they are not obedient to digestion by medicines, and use accelerates their digestion: then a hollow cauterization of fire, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that the smoke may go out from the cauterization at one extremity: and put fire on it above the aposteme once, and a second time, if you judge it necessary, until it penetrates to the depth of the aposteme.
Which if the aposteme is small: then put the cauterization according to the quantity of the aposteme.
Then leave it for three days, and put on it a plaster under butter, until there is removed what the fire burned.
Then treat it with toothpaste ointment, until it heals in the form of the cannula.
Of the method of cauterizing for roughness of the voice, and constriction of the breathing.
When the humidities flow over the canal of the lung, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the weak one be evacuated first with solvent medicines.
Then cauterize it in a nostril at the root of the throat in a depressed place: and beware, lest you penetrate with the cauterization to the throat, nor into the skin, except for a little of it.
Then cauterize it with a cautery at the junction of the neck on the last vertebra, applying it from below: and let the cautery be a moderate one, in the manner that has been described before.
Then treat it with what has been described before, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the Lung and Cough.
When the cough and disease of the lung are due to cold humidities, and the patient has no fever, nor phthisis, nor an old disease: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the armpit in depressed, gentle, empty places. And cauterize with another on the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be a reed one, according to the form that has been described before.
And if you need to cauterize by pricking with a cautery, which is called a Point, whose form has been described before in the pricking of ear pain: and let the points be from thirty points up to almost sixty.
Then treat it with what has been described before, until it is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches, according to this form. For it is alleviated by this cauterization, when you make with it one of three cauteries.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the joint is dislocated due to an excess of humidity, and it does not return to its place immediately after its dislocation, until it becomes accustomed to returning from its dislocation, then it becomes dislocated by a slight movement, which occurs as we have already testified, then you ought to reduce the dislocation first. Then let the patient lie on his back, or on his healthy side. Then elevate the cut which is inside the Titillici upwards with the fingers of your left hand and if the joint becomes dislocated inwards.
Then hold the cauterization iron with two fingers. Its shape is like this.
Then cauterize the cut until it penetrates to the other side and the figure of cauterization appears with four cauterizations.
And when the cauterization is done with a cauterizer having three fingers, then the figure of cauterization is made with six cauterizations: and they are fingers according to the subtlety attempted.
And this is the shape of a cauterizer having three fingers.
And when one is added to it in this manner, then there are eight cauterizations.
Then put on the cauterization ground pork with salt. Then make the weakened part adhere to quietness, so that it is not moved for a period of time, until it becomes strong.
And if the dislocation is upwards and it rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a cauterizer for the shoulder or with many punctures.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed: and the weak part is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the Stomach.
When many colds and moistures occur in the Stomach, until they extract it from its complex and multiply the catarrhs to it, and frequent modes of curation, and do not strengthen: then it is necessary that the weak one lies on his back, and stretches out his legs, and hands. Then cauterize with three cauterizations, one cauterizer under the cochlear of the breast, the size of one finger, with the shoulder cauterizer, and two cauterizations below by the two sides of one cauterizer, until the triangular figure of the cauterizations appears. And let it be extended between both so that they do not come together when they produce pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition, and if you use a large cautery on the middle of the stomach according to this form, and let the cautery that makes this cautery be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking him who trembles at this cautery, and it is, that you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity that you use with the encaustic, then cauterize it with the cautery of the point, then cure it with the curation which preceded until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When there is pain in the liver from cold and moisture, or from a gross flatulence, until it goes out from its natural passage, and the weak one is treated with what we have said, and does not profit from it: then it is necessary that the weak one breathe on his neck, and you mark with encaustic three cauteries according to this figure, and the same quantity on the lower liver below the hypocondriac region, where the elbow of a man penetrates: and let the space that is between each cauterium be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cauterium be straight in length according to the body: and do not press your hand with the cauterium much.
And let the quantity of what is burned be from the thickness of the skin, the quantity of its half not added, and let the weak one stand on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him be lying, who has already extended his legs and lifted up his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauterizations with a knife cautery, when there is subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware, that you do not proceed to the extreme in cauterization, and the thickness of the entire skin is burned, where the entire body is burned, and it penetrates to the intestines: for the skin there is delicate, therefore know that.
On the method of cauterizing apostemes of the liver.
When there occurs an exit wound, and you want to know if that apostema is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, a weak pain and heaviness without sharpness invade: and if it is in the tunic of the liver, with pain there is vehement sharpness: and you see already that it has wearied its physicians with treatment.
It is necessary therefore that the weak man breathes upon his neck. Then figure the place of the apostema with a searing heat: then ignite a cautery which is similar to a hot branding iron. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the entire skin is burned, and it penetrates to the siphac, until all the pus comes out: then treat it with the treatment of exit wounds, until it is healed.
And it is not necessary that this species of cautery be used, except by one whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands these diseases run with experimentation many times: then indeed he dares to undertake an operation of this kind.
But to leave it, with me it is better.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of Pleurisy.
The ancients said, a cautery with the roots of aristolochia for a cold Pleurisy in this manner. And it is, that you take from the roots of the dry long aristolochia, one root which is longer and found on it, and is as thick as a finger. Then submerge it in oil: and ignite it in the fire. Then cauterize with one cautery at the place which is between the junction of the jaw and the neck, and with two small cauteries slightly sloping downwards towards the part that is under the beard.
And with two cauteries also at the place which is between the fifth and sixth ribs sloping downwards towards the back a little: and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries on the back: one at the place which is between the two shoulder blades: and two cauteries on the two sides of the chest, below the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the cautery, unless it be on the manifest skin with a foul smell.
And certain ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron similar to a probe: and they ignite it, and insert it inside between the ribs, until it reaches with it to the apostema itself, and the pus comes out: as we have said concerning the apostema of the pleura.
But in this perforation with a cautery there is fear that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no cure.
On the method of cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the disease of the spleen, with that which we have said concerning the cure in the division of diseases, and your treatment is not effective, then a cautery on it is according to three methods, all of which are correct.
Of these one is, that you make three or four cauteries along the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauteries of the pleura, whose figure has preceded.
And let there be between the cautery a quantity of the thickness of a finger, or a little more.
And let the method of the cautery be that which we have described for the cautery of the liver equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery, and let the patient lean weakly on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: as we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder, to hold two rods of a fiery cautery, and to raise the skin which is along the spleen, where the weak left elbow penetrates: and let your elevation be such that you raise the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two ignited rods well in, until you penetrate the skin with them from the other side: then extract the cautery: thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three rods.
Then take care that the cautery, after you apply it, discharges pus for many days: for it is more conducive to healing than all the other things which have preceded in the cure.
On the method of cauterizing in Dropsy.
The cautery does not fall into a case of dropsy, except for a proper ascites.
When you treat a case of dropsy with the methods of cure which we have described in the division, and the cure is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery on the stomach, and another cautery on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two cauteries on the back between the spine, and one along the breast, and another along the stomach: and let the quantity of the depth of the cautery be near to the thickness of the skin.
Then diminish the open cauterization so that it emits pus over a long period.
And the weak should not be evacuated from the cure after the cauterization with what is necessary so that two intentions are added to it, and the healing will hasten with the help of God.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be a clamp, according to the form that preceded it: and that with which the back is cauterized, an olive, according to the form that preceded it.
On the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When they have apostemed in a hydropic and are filled with citrine water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the nocturnal, which is between the ear and the ring finger: and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then raise your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For the citrine water will flow out, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Then make on the two legs two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the extremity of the knife's edge: and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee and another lower than that, around the middle of the leg: and on the entire thigh make two cauteries: and diminish the open cautery without cure for a long time: so that some water flows out from it: then cure it with the remaining things that we have said.
On the method of cauterizing for the relief of the belly.
Chapter 35.
When there is a solution of the belly from cold and humidities, until it debilitates the retaining and digestive virtues, which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is cured with modes of cure, and not healed: and you see the weak one tolerating the cautery of abundant virtue, then cauterize it with a great cautery on its stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with the circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle clamp cautery: and a great cautery above the alcatin above the hump, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive humidity and the weak patient tolerating it, then cauterize it with a cauterizer over the chest, and cauterize everything with it: and perhaps you will add two small cauterizations over the stomach near the large one.
It is indeed a advancing treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they are from gross humors, cold, or corrupt humidities, and they are treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment is not effective: then cauterize with three cauterizations above the lower vertebra of the back under the alumidei for a short time in a triangular fashion, and cauterize under the navel almost two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face breaking out in a rash, then cauterize him over the stomach with a large cauterizer, according to what has preceded: and cauterize over his liver, and another over his spleen, with a cauterizer of the spine: and apply the open cauterization for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter 37.
When you remove a wart, then apply a cauterizer that resembles a radish. Then insert the ignited thing into the removed wart: and with your hand, until the cauterizer penetrates to the opening of the vein, from which blood runs: do it once, or twice.
If there are many warts, then cauterize each one with a cauterizer according to what we have described. Then treat them with that which is beneficial to them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize him with a large cauterization on the shoulder, it is more so in the joint.
Of the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the weak one does not undergo the cutting and operation that we described in its own place, and is deterred by it, perhaps he will be healed with a cauterization.
When therefore a fistula occurs to someone, and it becomes chronic, pus runs out of it, and corrupted moistures. It is fitting therefore that which ought to be done, that you should examine it with a subtle probe. Then recognize the quantity of its depth with a probe.
Then apply a cautery iron, which is similar to a probe. Then insert the ignited instrument itself into the fistula and the quantity in which the nail entered.
And repeat the cautery over it, until all those corrupted bodies are burnt, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of your necessity.
And beware of the burning of the nerve, if it is there, or of the great vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And do not do that, unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think, that it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
If however the place becomes closed, and matter is cut off from it, and it remains thus for a long time: then know that it is already healed completely.
And if matter is not cut off from it, then know that it is penetrating, or in its depth there is a corrupted opening, or something like that: the reminder of which will come in its own place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When there is pain in the kidneys from cold or from gross flatulence and it becomes weaker because of that, then it is necessary to cauterize it on the almethen over the kidneys themselves, to cauterize each kidney with a cauterizing iron, whose description has preceded.
And perhaps we will cauterize it a second time on that same almethen. Three linear scars will appear. Therefore, the last ones will be more in the flank.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When there is weakness in the bladder and softening from cold and humidity, until it does not retain weak urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the pubic area over the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and cauterize with one cauterizing iron on the right side of the pubic area, and another on the left side: and let the length of that cauterization be according to the quantity of a knot of the thumb: and cauterize it with a lower back cauterizing iron, or two cauterizing irons, if you judge it necessary: and let it be according to what has preceded, the cauterizing iron of the clavicle.
On the method of cauterizing the uterus.
When there is cold and humidity in the uterus, and it is prevented from conception because of that, and its menses are corrupted, and the provocation of them is delayed, and pain happens to it at the time of their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize with three cauterizing irons around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and cauterize over the lower abdomen with a back cauterizing iron, or two cauterizing irons: and let the cauterizing iron be of the clavicle.
On the method of cauterizing an ankle in a state of dislocation.
When the mucous humidities are poured out to the ankle's box, and they become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg is longer than the other when they are compared together: and the place of dislocation is found vacant in it.
It is necessary therefore that you cauterize the weak place above the ankle's box with a similar circular cautery: after which you mark with a branding iron around the circumference of the box, as it turns out: and so that the box itself falls in the middle of the circle.
Which if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive-tree cautery: and let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of the thickness of the whole skin.
Then treat it, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for sciatica.
When pain occurs in the box of the ankle, and the causes of it are cold and humidities: and the weak place is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and it becomes worse: then it is necessary that you release the weak place from gross humors with fetid pills, or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cautery in it is according to two methods: either a cautery with adhering medicines, or a cautery with fire.
The cautery with fire is according to many methods.
Of which one is, that you cauterize above the ankle's box with three triangular cauteries, according to this shape. And make for them a good depth, or a bad one. And let the space that is between all cautery be of the quantity of the thickness of the finger, and let the cautery be of olive.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the same ankle. There are four cauteries.
And if you apply the cautery with a circle, whose shape has preceded in the dislocation of the ankle, to one: so that the circle contains the whole ankle.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of the cautery for sciatica, when the pain adheres to the ankle itself, and does not extend to the hip and the leg.
If it extends to the hip and the leg, then apply the cautery with two cauteries above the hip, above the place to which that weakness points, in which is the pain, and apply your cautery above the haunch four fingers towards the wooded area for a short time: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
Which if the weakness indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then apply the cautery there where it points with a cautery of one point, or three, or four, or more, if it needs it.
And if it points to the pain being under the knee turned to the leg, then apply the cautery there with one knife-shaped cautery.
And beware in every cautery of yours, that you do not apply the cautery to this, so that you burn a nerve, or a large artery, and draw through it above the weakness a bad nocument, or contraction.
And I have already seen one and another, of those who applied the cautery above the haunch, and finished in the cautery, and the leg became inflamed, until a tumor followed to the foot, and it was entirely perforated, and the entire foot was corrupted: then there occurred a loosening of the belly, and death after that.
What if the pain is in two parts at the same time, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men have said regarding cauterization of the ankle, whose cauterization this is the method. Make a similar iron instrument, the diameter of which is half a palm, and let it be at its orifice according to the thickness of a date stone, or a little less, and inside that instrument let there be a third instrument.
And let the space that is between all the instruments be the size of a thumb joint, and let the instruments be open on two sides, and let their height be like a knot, or two knots, and make for them a handle from iron decently fitted to the instruments.
Then let it be ignited in the fire until it becomes red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed on a weak ankle, having reclined on the healthy side. Cauterize it therefore with three round cauterizations in one spot.
Then leave it for three days. Afterwards apply a plaster with butter, and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment, until it is healed.
Albucasis says, we have made little use of this type of cauterization, on account of the terror of its appearance, and because we find few who dare to try it.
However, it is one of the good cauterizations for him who suffers it and finds its place.
A cauterization with adhering medicines is to make two instruments having a perforated armlet, into which descends a rod of the door of bronze or iron, the length of a wall, and for their height there are two knots, or nearly so.
And let the space that is between both be the size of a finger's thickness, and let it be open below and above, and let what they contain be joined to each other, according to this form.
Then remove it and place it on a plaster bandage, the weak lying on the healthy side. And press your hand strongly on the plaster bandage. Then pour between the two circles from warm water, which has been heated with fire for a short time, and hold it for an hour's quantity of time: and let the weak endure its biting and burning, for he finds the biting as fire, until the biting subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wipe away the warm water from the entire bandage with sweet water: then leave it for three days.
And put on it butter, until the blackness of the burn is removed: and leave it for several days, and pus will be cured from it. It is indeed the last in the treatment.
Then treat it with ointments, until it is healed.
What if the pain extends to the hip or the leg: make for it a plaster that contains water, according to what you did on the bandage equally.
And this is the method of warm water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take of alkaline substance and unslaked lime each one part: grind both, and put them in a new pot, the lower part of which is perforated with one small hole, according to the quantity that the radius may enter: and put under the bottom of the pot another pot vitreous: and throw over the alkaline substance and lime sweet water, which submerges both by the finger: after which you compress it with your hand with good compression: and leave the pot until sharp water descends to the lower part of the vitreous pot.
Then collect that water entirely, and throw it over another lime: and filter, until it is renewed.
It itself will then be of strong sharpness indeed, which is administered in many operations of medicine, and in the cauterization of the remaining members. Since it performs the operation of its own fire.
And there are medicines with which they cauterize the anch, and also such as tessie, and honey of the anacard, and lime with soap, so that both may be mixed together.
And Galen told of a certain man from the ancients, whose cure was for the pain of the ankle and the vein of the thigh, and he declared its effectiveness to be very great. And he said that it did not need another cure, and that he was healed by one remedy, until he related that he perhaps entered a bath and came out of it already healed.
And it is, that it be taken from the green vitriol, and if the green is not found, let the dry, fresh one be taken, and let it be ground much with some fat, and let it be put on the ankle, where there is pain, or the leg, or in the hip, and let it be tied, and let it be left for the quantity of three hours, or as long as he feels the weakness of the heat of the application. Then let him enter into a bath.
When therefore his body becomes very sweaty, let him enter into the sun. For the pain recedes and he is healed.
And know that it is not necessary to use any cauterization with these medicines, unless after the purging of the body.
And Dioscorides said that the dung of capers, when with it the vein of the thigh is cauterized, brings to it relief, and makes a cauterization in this manner. Let wool be ground, and let it be soaked with old oil, and let it be put on the deep place, which is between the thumb of the foot, and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take dry dung of a goat and set it on fire, until it becomes charcoal.
Then put it on a cloth and let it be, until it is extinguished. Then repeat that. Do not stop doing that until the sensation on the middle and up to the ankle is penetrated and the pain subsides.
And this method of cauterization is called the cauterization of the cow.
Of the cauterization of pain in the back.
When pain occurs in the back for many reasons, or from a fall, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and damp material: and cauterization is not applied, except in this single case, which occurs from the infusion of cold material.
It is necessary therefore after evacuation of the weak with fetid pills and similar things, so that they make on the back, where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the affected part, then mark with a cautery in each line five cauterizations, or more according to the quantity that comes from the tolerance of the weak, by virtue of which: and let the cauterization be made with cauterized points.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauterizations, with the middle clavicular cautery, according to this method.
Of the method of cauterizing in cases of gibbosity.
This sickness often happens to small infants.
And the sign of this disease in children is: that there occurs a tightening on it with shortness of breath at elevation and movement: and you find in the last vertebrae of the back and its knots, which already begins to protrude over the remaining vertebrae.
When I raise that and make a use for it, then I cauterize it with a cauterizer that is a circle according to this form.
And let the cauterization take hold equally over every part of the vertebrae: and if you cauterize around the vertebrae with a pointed cauterizer two or three lines: and let the points be close to one another.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you administer a cauterization on a hump that forms in a spasm of a nerve.
On the method of cauterizing for gout and joint pains.
When joint pains are from cold humidities that flow to any members of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is by custom of physicians to name that specifically Gout.
When therefore gout caused by cold is treated with methods of cure and the pains are not removed, then a cauterization removes them.
And it is that you cauterize after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cauterizers: and let the cauterization be with an oily one.
And if you indicate that there are points on the surface of the foot, then make them with a pointed cauterizer. Which if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints and it often happens, then cauterize it above every knee with three or four cauterizers on every side, with this same cauterizer of the ankle.
If however many are needed for you with this cauterizer, then cauterize it. And do not submerge your hand with the cauterizer, but rather let it be to the thickness of the skin as much.
If however pains ascend to the knees and the back: then administer what we have said from cauterization in its chapter.
What if pains are in the hands only, then puncture at the circuit of the elbow joints, as two lines turn.
If however there remains from pains in the fingers, then puncture them, above every joint a puncture, and above the palm of the hand.
If however pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not evacuate the weak from a good regime, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regime is made, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God by this cauterization.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of rupture.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and intestine descends, or a cyst to the testicle, and it is beginning nearby: then it is necessary to prescribe to the weak that they abstain from food on that day. And let him use laxatives, so that feces may descend from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and prescribe to him, that he hold his breath, until it comes out, or the cyst appears, or intestine.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a cauterizing iron under the rupture on the bone of the hip, with a mark whose extremities are similar to the middle of a circle towards the upper parts of the body.
Then ignite the cauterizing iron, which has this form, until it becomes white, and throws out sparks. Then reduce the intestine or cyst to its concavity. Then let the servant put his hand on the place, so that the intestine does not come out: and you have already opened between the thighs of the weak, and placed under it a pillow, and one servant over the thighs of him, and another over his chest who holds the hands.
Then apply the cautery on the same sign, your hand with the cautery standing upright. And hold it until you bring it to the mouth, or turn it with it twice, if you have not brought it to the mouth at first.
And carefully observe from the intestine's exit at the time of your cauterization, lest you burn it, and an issue comes through that above the weak or mortified place, or great malignity.
And know that when you do not bring the cautery to the mouth, your operation is of no use.
And it is fitting that the cautery for infants be subtle, according to their measure.
Then treat with the remaining ointments, until it is healed.
And let the weak one lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is closed.
And it is fitting that you put a nourishment for it for the length of time of its cure, which will soothe its stomach: so that the intestine does not come out through the wound and vomiting.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let him hold it for forty more days.
And he should be kept from labor, and from the filling of food and drink, and vehement voices.
For when he uses this regime, thus will he be healed with a complete healing.
And I will speak of the cure of hernias with an incision in its own chapter.
When however hernias occur in the remaining abdomen, and are beginning, and it is seen that they do not increase, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its quantity: and let what is applied be about one third of it. Then treat it with what we have said: and it will not increase.
And now some of the first have said: that a hernia should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a cautery, and a line is placed which runs along the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line to the lower one. And put your hand in the middle with the cautery on the hip.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
On the method of cauterizing for pains caused by a fall or a blow.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in certain members from a fall or a blow, and the pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines is of no benefit, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of each member be a second cautery according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting and pain from it.
If therefore it is healed by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then repeat it over the same cautery.
For it is a habit of these pains that they are transferred from one member to the one that is nearest to it. Wherefore it is necessary to follow them with a cautery until the weak part is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes helped by a very strong cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: when therefore you want to cauterize it, consider it.
If therefore the leprosy is beginning, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it does not decrease, nor stop: and there is a weak spot that corruption has comprehended over its whole complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one on the middle of the head at the knot, and a second below that towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally touch your hand briefly with the cautery, until it impresses a small mark on the mouth, and the cortices will dislocate from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors is eased from it, and cauterize with the cautery also above the same spleen, according to what has proceeded.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the weak part, and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with those cauteries, which we mentioned in the beginning, and cauterize above the extremity of the nose, and with two cauteries above the two jaws, and with two cauteries above the vertebrae of the neck, and six above the vertebrae of the back, and one large one above the region of the tail near the end of the spine and one above it, in the same flank: and two above the elbows: namely one above each elbow, and two above the knees: one above each knee, and two above the shoulders, and two above the elbows, and two above the tenderness of his chest: and cauterize it above every joint, of the joints of his fingers and toes: and cauterize above every heel of his feet, and the soles of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes cauterization is performed with a cautery on the bone of the chest, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater is the benefit, and the more it helps.
And know that the weak person does not find pain in the cautery, as the healthy ones do: because his body is already numbed.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of a size and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to what has preceded from the species of iron instruments.
Then treat with a cauterization made from powder of the herb with honey, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for a stupor.
When any member is numb, and it is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterize the numb member with cauterizations, according to what its size deserves or its smallness.
And let your cauterization penetrate briefly into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
And when the cauterization is applied for a numbness that occurs to the hand and foot, at the joints of the back near where the nerves exit, which move that member: and the numbness is removed.
Indeed, let no one presume to do this except one who is wise in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter 51.
When the Baras becomes chronic and nothing from the ingenuity of medicine is effective for it: then cauterize over it with a deep cauterization briefly, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with powder of the herb and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of a pigeon, and blood of a hyrundine: let each be one part: mix all these things, and apply them to a cloth, and adhere to the place, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for a Cancer.
When the Cancer is beginning and you want to restrain it: then cauterize it with a circular cauterization around its circumference, as it revolves.
Wise men have said that a cauterization should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
It does not seem to me: because I fear that it will become an ulcer, and I have already seen that happen many times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we have said, or with many cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of boils.
When someone has a boil and it is delayed in maturing, either because of the excess matter that makes it, or because of the weakness of the patient, when he is decrepit and has little blood, or because of the time and the need to hasten the maturation of the boil, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, making many punctures. Then leave it alone. For it will hasten the maturation by itself.
If you want to make a perforation of it with a cautery, then ignite the cautery, whose shape is this.
And place it in the middle of the boil, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be made from that which follows, being weak, so that the flow of pus may be alleviated.
Then treat it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for a corroding sore.
Chapter 54.
A corroding sore is nothing but a corruption that moves in a member and corrodes it: just as fire devours dry wood.
