Sometimes there occurs under the tongue an aposteme resembling a small frog, which prevents the tongue from performing its natural function, and perhaps grows to such an extent that it fills the mouth.
And the operation for this is to open the mouth of the invalid before you, and examine the aposteme.
If you see that it is of a dark or black color, and hard, and the invalid has lost sensation in it, then do not touch it, because it is a cancer.
And if it inclines to whiteness, in which there is moisture, then apply a hook to it, and cut it with a subtle spatula, and free it from every part. What if blood gushes out during your operation, then put over it pounded alum, until the bleeding stops: then return to your operation, until you extract it with its appendage.
Then let it be cleansed with vinegar and salt: and treat it with the rest of the treatment suitable for that, until it is healed.
On the cure of an aposteme of two tonsils.
Chapter 36.
Sometimes there occur in the throat two glands, that is, tonsils, which resemble two almonds, which occur at the back of the throat: and are called two Amigdalae: which when you treat with what we have said in the division, and they do not heal, then consider.
If it is a hard aposteme, of dark color, with little sensation, then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of a red color, and its root is thick, then do not touch it with iron either, fearing a flow of blood, but rather leave it alone until it matures. And then either you will perforate it or it will rupture by itself.
And if it is white in color, round, and its root is subtle: then it should be cut.
And the operation on it is, that you consider before its operation, if the apostema of its tumor has completed quiet heat, or is diminished by some diminution: then make the weak sit in front of the sun, and its head be in your bosom: and open its mouth, and the servant receives between his hands, and presses its tongue below with an instrument, which has this form.
Let it be made from silver, or copper, which is subtle like a knife.
When I press the tongue with it, and the tumor is shown to you, and your sight falls upon it: then take a hook, and fix it in the tonsil, and extract it to the exterior as much as you can, except that you draw with it something from the tunics.
Then cut it with an instrument, which has this form that follows. It is assimilated to forceps: nevertheless its extremities are curved, so that the orifice of each of them is directly opposite the other's point: hence take care that it be made from iron or tempered steel.
If however this instrument is not at hand, then cut it with a spatula, which has this form. Let it be sharp on one side, not sharp on the other side.
And after you cut one tonsil, cut the other according to this same species of cutting.
Then after the cutting, let the weak person gargle with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
If however there happens to him a flow of blood, let him gargle with water in which the barks of pomegranates have been boiled: or leaves of myrtle, and similar things from astringents, until the flow of blood is stopped: then take care of him, until he is healed.
And whenever abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils. Cut them therefore equally as I have said in the cutting of the two tonsils.
And I indeed have already treated a woman for an abscess that had formed in her throat, which was pulling towards the trachea, with little sensation, which had almost closed her throat: and the woman was breathing through a narrow passage, and it had already forbidden her both food and water: and she would have reached death, if she had remained one day or two days.
And the abscess had risen so much that it had sent out two branches, until they went out above the two nostrils.
I proceeded therefore with haste, and I fixed a hook on one of them. Then I pulled it, and a large portion was pulled out from it.
Then I cut it off, where it was grasped coming out of the nostril.
Then I did to it what had come out of the other nostril.
Then I opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue: and afterwards I fixed a hook into the abscess: then I cut off from it a part of it, and there did not flow out from it except a little blood: therefore the throat of the woman was cured, and she began at once to drink water, then she took some food.
I did not therefore cease to cut into that abscess many times for a long time: and the abscess was succeeding in the place of what I had cut, until it was prolonged too much and with it.
I heated therefore, and cauterized the abscess in the throat.
It stood therefore from increasing: then I walked away from the place, and I did not know what God did with it after me.
Of the cutting of the abscess of the uvula.
Chapter 37.
When the cold descends to the gum and becomes an abscess and is long: then it itself is called perpendicular: and if it is in the lower part thick, round, then it itself is called a gum boil.
When it is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not work: and you see that the hot abscess has quieted from it, and is subtle: then it is necessary to cut it.
And that which is gathered from it round, and is not in length, and is bloody, or of a dark reddish color, or black, and has no sensation: then it is necessary to avoid cutting it. For there is fear regarding the weak place.
It is necessary therefore when you see it according to the measure which I spoke of from its whiteness, and its length, that you make the weak one sit before the sun: and press its tongue with an instrument, whose description has preceded: then fix a hook in the gum, and pull it downwards: and cut it with one of the two instruments which I have spoken of in the cutting of the two tonsils.
And it is necessary that you do not cut from it, except that which is added beyond the natural limit without addition.
For if you cut from it more, you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after the cutting use that which we have described in the cutting of the two tonsils: and treat it, until it is healed.
If however the weak one trembles from the cutting: then it is necessary that you use skill in cauterizing it without fear and trembling.
And the method of cauterization on it is not, except with sharp water: and it is, that you put the head of the weak one in your lap. Then press its tongue with the instrument which we mentioned. Then take from the water which I told you about in the chapter on cauterization, and mix it with lime that is not extinguished, and put it not thick, nor subtle, and fill with it the concavity of this instrument, whose form is this.
Let the extremities of it in which the medicine is placed be hollow, like the hollow of a spoon.
And put the instrument with the medicine on the wound itself: and let the weak person be lying on their side, so that saliva runs out of their mouth from the inward medicine, so that nothing from it descends to their throat, and harms them.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you apply it to the wound for the first time in the quantity of a half hour, until you see that it is already blackened and the biting of the medicine has sat.
And if you want to take a piece of cloth, and wrap it around the extremity of the radius, and dip the cloth in medicine, and insert the radius with the cloth into the tube above, until the cloth adheres to the wound.
Do that many times, until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the wound. Then leave it alone: for it will dry out and fall off after three days, or four.
What if you judge that you should repeat the medicine, repeat it: and after cauterization cleanse around the wound with a cloth soaked in butter, and purify what is around it from the medicine: and wash with cold water.
And let it be treated outwardly with poultices, and inwardly with gargles, until it is healed.
This species of cure is healthier than incision and less frightening.
And sometimes the wound is treated with what is more subtle than cauterization and incision: for it is treated with fumigation, in this manner. Take calamentum, and hyssopum, and origanum, and rue, and ssacah, and chamomile, and abrotanum, and similar things from the herbs: and gather all of them, or some of them in a pot, and submerge them with vinegar, and boil: and let the pot be covered with a decent lute: and let there be in the middle of the pot an opening, over which an instrument concave is placed according to this method.
Let it be made from silver, or bronze: and the extremity is introduced, in which there is a grain, into the mouth of the infirm, until the vapor ascends to the palate over the tube, until the palate becomes very obscured.
Then let it be rubbed repeatedly over the same spot, until it is scratched.
And beware, lest you make this cure at the beginning of the appearance of the apostema. For a plaster adds to the apostema: and it is not necessary that you do that unless at the decline of the heat of the apostema.
If however this instrument is not present to you, then take a cane, and place the bark of an oak on the extremity of it: so that the mouth of the infirm does not become scorched: for the bark of the oak prevents the vapor from scorching the mouth: and this is from good cure with health.
Of the extraction of thorns, and bones from the jaw.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Many times a bone, or a fishbone, or something else sticks to the throat.
It is necessary therefore that you extract what of them is apparent on which the sight falls, after you press the tongue with an instrument at the seat, and it is revealed to you what is in the throat.
And what does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make the infirm vomit before it is digested by the foods in the stomach. For a foreign body will come out through vomiting.
Or let the weak person swallow a piece of nap, or a root of lettuce, or let him swallow a small piece of dry bread: or let him take a piece of dried sea sponge and tie it with a thread, then swallow it. When therefore it reaches the place where are the spine or bone, and is extracted, then it comes out.
If it does not come out with what we have said, then use an instrument made of lead according to this form.
Let it be thicker than a Rod a little, and at its end let there be a curvature, which it introduces into the throat with ease: and let it have its head elevated upwards.
And let it beware of the touch of its epiglottis, so that coughing does not happen to it, and let it push the mouth, or bone, or let the doctor introduce it with his hand.
But what the weak person introduces, this is better: on account of his knowledge of the place of the annexed thing: and he pushes downwards, or pulls his hand with an instrument upwards, all that according to the quantity which is prepared for him, until it comes out.
On the extraction of a bloodsucking creature.
Chapter 39.
When a bloodsucking creature is treated with what I said in the division on curation with medicines, and it does not work, then consider in the throat of the weak person before the sun, or at the sun after you press his tongue with an instrument that I have described to you.
If your sight then falls upon the bloodsucking creature, extract it with a small hook, or with delicate fingers.
What if it is not possible with these: then take a concave tube, and introduce it into the throat of the weak person until near the throat: then introduce into the concavity of the tube ignited iron with fire. Let him do that many times, and let the weak man abstain from water for the whole day.
Then let him take a full drink of cold water, and open his mouth in it, and let him spit out the water, and not swallow anything of it, and let him move the water with one hand after another. For a leech indeed falls when it feels the water.
If however it does not come out with what we have described, then fumigate the weak person with cemephis, or with ase with an instrument that I described for fumigating the womb.
Do that many times, because it itself will fall.
And the method of operation in fumigation is, that you take a pot, in which there are burning prunes of a womb with fire, and the pot is covered with a cover, in whose middle there is a hole, and let the end of the instrument be placed in that hole.
Then throw in the fumigation, and let the weak person put his mouth on the end of the cannula, and let him close his mouth, so that the fumigation does not come out, until you know that the fumigation has already reached the leech. For the leech will immediately fall.
Because if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times.
And let the weak person endure thirst, and eat salty things, and garlic, and not drink water.
It is necessary therefore that it comes out with this treatment.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the leech is extracted from the throat, when it falls onto the same sight.
It is similar to forceps, as you see, except that it has this curvature which is introduced into the throat. And its end is similar to a bird's beak, which is called cicoria, in which there is roughness of a file: when it grasps something, it does not release it at all.
On the opening of abscesses and their cutting and care in general.
Chapter 40.
There are many kinds of abscesses, of many modes, according to which the treatment of them is remembered, namely one, and one in this book: and they are diverse in the perforation of them, and their cutting from two modes.
Of which one is from the species of abscesses in itself, and that which it comprises of humors.
And the second mode is because of the places, in which it happens in the body.
For an abscess happening on the head is different from an abscess happening on the anus: and an abscess happening in a fleshy place is different from an abscess happening on the joints: and each of them has its own judgment from the operation.
And of the abscesses there are some which should not be perforated, unless after the maturation of the pus in them and its completion: and of them there are some which should be perforated while they are raw and do not mature according to completion.
Such as abscesses that are near the joints.
For when an abscess happens near a joint and its existence is prolonged until the putrefaction of what is in its surroundings perhaps corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, which is a cause of more likely contraction of that member.
Or it is an abscess near a principal member: for if you delay the perforation of it until it matures, it will harm either that or through that principal member.
Or it is near the anus, perforate it therefore while it is immature: and it is not necessary to perforate a raw abscess, of incomplete digestion, unless that which is near the anus, so that it does not putrefy deeply and extend to the interior of the anus, and become a fistula, or become in its termination what does not heal.
It is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the apostema, which has matured according to its completion: and it is at the sedation of pain, the recession of fever, and the diminution of redness, and pulsation, and the acuteness of the head of the apostema: and other signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower place of the apostema, and of the more prominent elevation: and let the perforation be going in the length of the body, if the apostemata are in the parts of the hands and feet, and the places of the armpits, and tendons, and nerves, and arteries, and at last in all equal places, to which there is not a reflexion.
In those however which are reflected, let it go with the perforation according to that membrane.
When the apostema is in fleshy places, then it is better that you omit its perforation, until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to its completion.
For if you perforate it before that, the course of the pus is prolonged from it, and there is much filth and foulness, and perhaps the lips of it will become hardened, and its depth.
And some apostemata are perforated according to the width of the body, by necessity: or according to that which the membrane needs.
And it is necessary that you administer in small apostemata a small perforation, and in large apostemata a large perforation: or many sections by similarity of the magnitude of the apostema.
And there are of the apostemata, in which it is necessary that the skin be concave: and let it be cut when already it has been made like a cloth, and it has been made at the end, which already is dead: as that which happens to many, such as buboes and dubelles.
And of them there are those which cut with a section having three angles. And from them is that from which an incision is made as the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Like an abscess in the groin.
And from them are those in which a round incision and a crescent-shaped incision are administered, and similar to them from the incisions.
That one indeed which has no head, as are lenient superficial abscesses, ought to be pierced by a superficial piercing, or only a flat one.
And it is necessary, when the abscess is thick, and has already collected much purulent matter, and you pierce it, that you not hurry and extract all the pus at that hour: but rather extract a part of it from it. Then stop up the abscess until another day. Then extract something from the pus again.
Do that many times according to the gradation, until it goes out: especially if he is weak and of little strength, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man: for the vital spirit is often resolved from the animal with the going out of pus: and perhaps the weak person dies, and you do not perceive.
Beware therefore this chapter with great caution.
And after your piercing, by which you pierce the abscesses, it is necessary that you cleanse the wound: and take care. If therefore the wound of the abscess is small, or is a flat incision, then administer dressings made from linen, or old cloth. And if the abscess is large, and there are many openings of the piercing, it is necessary then that you insert a dressing into every opening, until they reach the bottom.
And if you have cut away a part of the skin in the abscess, or have hollowed it out around: then it is necessary that you fill it with old cloth, or as when a fabric is woven, or wool from linen without moisture: and bind it until the third day.
Then anoint it, and treat it with what is necessary from the ointment, until it is healed.
And if there occurs a flow of blood during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar, after which the cloth is soaked in them: and you put it on the place of the flow of blood many times.
And if the flow of blood persists, then it is necessary that you administer a treatment and a cure and powders, which I have described in many places of this our book, and from division.
And if it is in the time of winter, and the place of the abscess is of many nerves: then it is necessary that you pour in powders with wine, and hot oil: and you put them on the places.
And if it is in summer, and the places are fleshy: then it is necessary that you put powders soaked in water, and oil, or wine and oil, and all of that is cold. Until when it will be the third day, as we have said, then it is necessary that you loosen the abscess, and clean it, and administer in its cure what is suitable for it, until it is healed.
This is therefore what is necessary from the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally.
According to the path of distinction, I have already spoken about every abscess, in what way it is a path to its cure, chapter by chapter, individually.
Chapter 41.
On the section of abscesses which occur on the skin of the head.
There occur on the skin of the head small abscesses, and they are of the species of Knots, which are contained in sacs, and these are attached to them: as if they themselves were husks of a hen.
And their species are many.
Some of them are fatty: and some of them contain humidity similar to slime: and some of them contain humidity similar to friction and poultices: and similar things, and some of them are hard stony.
And in the cutting of all, and their extraction, there is no fear, provided that in their cutting it does not cause a contrariness of the arteries.
And the operation in their cutting is that you try them with an instrument, whose form comes after this, which is called Intromissum, until you know what it contains.
For if it is that which contains humidity, then dry it by a cut according to the length of the superficial cut: according to this form.
And begin with a cut from line b to line g. When therefore the humidity is evacuated, then scratch out the cyst which contains that humidity, and do not leave anything of it deeply.
For it returns many times, if something of it remains.
Then submerge the wound in Egyptian ointment, if it is present: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the wound with it, and leave it until another day. For it corrodes what remains of the cyst.
Then repeat over the wound with Egyptian ointment a second and third time, and if you apply it to it, until you are confident that nothing remains of the cyst, then treat the wound with ointment, until it is healed.
What if the apostema contains a fatty knot: then cut it according to this form, having the form of a cross: and apply ointment between the lips of the incision, and scratch it out from every part: and examine your skill in the extraction of the tunic which contains it.
If however the artery makes a contrariness to you, then do that which I will tell you afterwards.
And do similarly in the case of a stone, from cutting and cure, the same as we have said.
And the cutting over a stone apostema is easier: since there is little blood and humidity. And whenever there are certain apostemata which are on the head in certain men, with which there is not deep humidity.
Which is: that I cut into an apostema on the head of an old woman, and I found the apostema like a solid and hard stone, rough, white, which could not be broken: and if anyone were to strike it by throwing something at it, it would wound.
In other accidental apostemata on the head, apart from these, namely the apostemata which occur on the heads of boys, and at the roots of the ears, let the dissection of all of them be a superficial dissection.
Or make a perforation of them always from the lower part of them, so that the flow of blood may be alleviated to the lower parts.
Then treat it with what is suitable for it from the treatment.
On the dissection of Tumors on the neck.
Chapter 42.
These apostemata often occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groins: and sometimes they occur on the rest of the body.
And above those which occur on the neck, there is one, and many: and they are generated from the nearby area: and every tumor of them is inside its own proper tunic, as it is in knots and apostemata of the head, as we have described.
And there are many kinds of these Tumors. And among them are some that are stony: and among them are those which contain humors: and among them are malignant ones, which do not obey treatment.
Therefore, in that one which you see among them of good disposition to the touch, whose manifest proximity is to the color of the skin, and it moves in every part, and it is not attached with the nerves of the neck, nor with the gullet, nor with the artery, nor is it deep: it is necessary that you dissect it with a superficial dissection from the upper part to the lower part of the body along the line, and along the line, and extract it from every part: and extend the two lips of the skin with a hook, or with many hooks, if you need them, as we have said in the case of apostemata of the head, and extract it little by little.
And it is above the caution, that the vein or nerve is not cut.
And let the spatula be not sharp, so that it does not add your hand to the incision, or disturb the weak, and cut what is not necessary.
If you cut the vein, or artery, it prohibits you from operation, then put on the wound pounded zegi, or some powders that absorb blood, and tighten the wound, and leave it, until the sharpness of the swelling subsides, and the wound softens: or it begins to putrefy.
For blood is absorbed by a tunic of flesh, therefore return to your operation, until you finish.
Then examine with your index finger, if anything remains of the small spurs: therefore cut them, and clean them.
What if there is in the root of the spur a large vein: then it is necessary that you do not cut that spur from its root: but rather it is necessary that you tie it with a double strong thread, and leave it until it falls off by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with old cotton, which you have already steeped in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of it.
If the entire spur is cut, then it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound: and sew them immediately, after which you see that nothing protrudes in excess.
If you see that something remains in excess because of the size of the spur, then it is necessary that you proceed to cut its root, and extract it: and administer the suture which we mentioned.
And what of the spurs contains humidity, pierce it with a superficial piercing: so that the place of its maturation appears to you: and put the piercing from that which follows below the body, as we said.
Then administer a dressing with an ointment after the perforation, and similar things to it, so that it corrodes what remains from the corruption, until when you see the wound is already clean: then treat it with a generating ointment of flesh, until it is healed.
Chapter 43.
Of the cutting of the epiglottis by an abscess that occurs within the throat.
The ancients spoke of this incision on the Epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has performed it: and this is the writing of their speech.
However, in those having synanche, it is necessary that the incision of the Epiglottis be deviated: since no passage can be made through it: because all the veins and the lung are weak.
In those indeed who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or throat, or both tonsils, when there is no illness in the canal, it is necessary to use the incision of the Epiglottis, to flee from the destruction which is made by the suffocation.
It is necessary therefore when we wish it, that we cut the Epiglottis under three circles of the Epiglottis, or four, a small incision in width, in what is between two circles in quantity, so that the incision is in the sifac, not in the cartilage: and this place indeed is convenient for the incision, because it is deprived of flesh, and the vessels of blood from it are distant.
What if the doctor is timid, then it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat with a hook. Then let him pierce the skin, until when he reaches the canal: let him divert the vessels of blood, if he sees any of them.
Then let him cut the sifac which we have described: and it is indicated above the incision of the canal from the phlegm that exits from it, with what disrupts it, and from the cutting off of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
When the hour arrives in which the anointing is feared, bring together the two lips of the wound of the skin, and suture it itself alone without cartilage.
Then administer medications which make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Said Albucasis. The sum of this speech which we have narrated is not an exposition, except when they see that one of these apostemata has already strangled the throat of the weak; and the weak has been lifted up from death, and his breaths are about to be cut off: they proceed to cut the Epiglottis, so that the weak may breathe over the place of the wound by some breathing, and may be saved from death: and for this reason they have ordered to leave the wound open, until the evil of the disease is consumed, and its evil is for three days, or thereabouts; then therefore they have ordered to suture the wound, and to treat it, until it is healed.
And that which I have seen with my own eyes is, that a certain servant girl took a knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut the part of the canal of the lung.
And I was called to the cure of her, and I found her to rattle, as is the rattling of the dead.
I probed therefore from the wound, and I found blood which had come out from the wound a little. I was confused therefore that she had not cut the vein, nor the trachea: and the air came out from the wound.
I treated therefore the wound and her wound, and I cured it, until it was sound: and nothing happened to the servant girl, except hoarseness of voice: and she returned after days to her better dispositions.
Hence therefore I say: that in the cutting of the Epiglottis there is no fear.
On the surgical incision of the throat hernia
Chapter 44
This condition called hernia of the throat, is a large abscess, secondary to body color, and it occurs frequently in women.
And it is secondary to two methods: for it is either natural or it is accidental.
In the natural one certainly there is no ingenuity.
The accidental one, however, is secondary to two methods: of which one is similar to fatty knots. And the other method is similar to an abscess that forms from a knotting of the artery. And in it there is fear, and it is not suitable that a presumption be made regarding it with iron, unless in that which is small: and you will examine it, and investigate it with an introduction. If therefore you find it similar to a fatty knot, and it is not suspended with any vein: then cut it, as knots are cut: and extract it with what it contains from the cyst, if it is in a cyst: and if not, then probe the whole of it. Then treat the place with what is proper for the cure, until it is healed.
Chapter 45
On the surgical incision of the type of knots.
There are many types of knots, and I have already mentioned all their types in the division: and it is necessary that I describe here the difference between a Knot and an Excrescence: since it causes doubt.
I say therefore, that when there is an Excrescence, there is heat, and fever, and vehement pains, until the ebullition of the surplus is satiated, and the putrefaction is complete: then indeed the fever and heat subside.
With a Knot, however, there is no heat, nor fever, nor pains, and it contains them in cysts, which is their proper sac, and it is secondary to body color: and its shape is like a seed, and it forms like a boil, and it is larger and smaller.
And they are divided into two types: either fatty or containing humidity. And the colors of humidity are many, according to what I said in division.
It is necessary therefore, when you come to the cure of a Knot, that you try it, and examine it first with an instrument which is called Intromissum, according to which its form will appear in the chapter which is after this.
And the method of examining abscesses and all Knots is that you take this instrument and insert it into the most humid place which you find in the abscess, and you move your fingers with it gradually until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the skin. Then you put your hand finally according to the measure of the size of the abscess.
Then you extract the Intromissum, and examine what comes out in its track.
If therefore a running humidity comes out, whatever the color may be: then dry it with a superficial incision, according to what I said concerning other abscesses.
And if humidity does not come out in the track of the Intromissum, then know that it is fatty: dry therefore above it with an incision having the form of a cross, according to this form, as I have taught you: and suspend it with hooks, and scratch the skin from every side with ease: and guard the kistin if you can above it, so that you extract it healthy with the Knot.
If however the kistis bursts during the operation, and it is not possible to extract it whole, for this often happens, then extract it by fragments, until nothing of it remains.
For if a little or much of it remains, the Knot returns according to the amount.
If it overcomes you and a little of it remains: then fill the wound at the completion with certain corrosive powders: and bind the wound, and put on top of it what sits on the abscess, a hot application, and treat it with the remaining cure, until it is healed.
If it is a large knot, then sew its two lips, and cure it with what flesh grows around it.
If there is a contrary vein, either pulsating or not pulsating: then press, and fill the place of the zegi with trito, and leave it tied for two days, or three, until the wound putrefies, and the ebullition of blood quiets down: afterwards return to cut that which remains of the Knot.
Chapter 46.
On the forms of instruments for cutting and boring.
These are the forms of the introdgers, and they are of three kinds.
For among them is a large one, and among them is a medium one, and among them is a small one.
Let them be made from iron of Al-fulud, a quadrangular shape at the extremities, so that they fasten the entry into the abscess.
And these are the forms of the Experients, and yes, that is, the perforators: and one of them is named beris, that is, the perforator: and they are of three kinds.
For among them is a large one, and a medium one, and a small one.
They are joined so that they investigate through them the abscesses and the exits and the fistulas and the buboes from what is between them of bones.
And others are made round, smooth, slender, like large needles with which they sew under the skin, namely of citrus, or of copper, or iron, or silver.
And the better ones of them are those that are made from citrus.
And they make the Experients also from black lead, which are joined so that through them they investigate the fistulas, whose concavities are reflections, so that they reflect with their slenderness together with those reflections.
And they are again of three kinds. Since some of them are long, some of them are medium, and some of them are short, according to the quantity of the width of the fistula and its stricture.
The forms of ulcers, and they are of many species.
Since some of them are simple, namely those which have one curvature: and they are of three species, as you see, Large, Medium, and Small.
And some of them are blind ulcers: and they are of three species.
And some of them are ulcers having two curvatures, and they are of three species: and some of them are ulcers having three curvatures, and they are of three species: and all of these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of scalpels, with which they cut and excavate knots and apostems: and they are of three species: since some of them are large, medium, and small.
Their extremities with which a section is made are acute, the other extremities are not acute: and they are not placed thus, except so that with them there is a judgment in the excavation of knots regarding the fear of cutting a vein, or nerve: and so that it may be healed by this, and it finds tranquility for a time from the burning which it found at the excavation of an apostem.
They are made of copper, and they are similar to a file, with which the file is sharpened: and on the broad extremity there is a point of Spatumilis hidden: and in it there runs to the interior and to the exterior when you wish, as you see.
The form of Spatumilis which are hidden between the fingers for the perforation of apostems: and the weak do not perceive them: and they are of three species, large, medium, and small.
The forms of cauteries with which the flow of blood is cut off: and they are of three species, large, medium, and small.
They should be made from bronze or brass, rounded, and a little long, as you see: and they should be to subtlety.
And it is fitting that you should have those kinds of large and small bloodletting instruments: so that you can cut blood with speed when necessary, and then when medicine is not present.
But you should not use them for bloodletting in every part of the body, and you should not use them except in fleshy places: such as the arms, thighs, hips, upper arms, breasts, belly, groin, and similar ones to these, from the fleshy arms, humid.
And sometimes small instruments similar to the rinds of gourds are made from them, according to their shape: with which blood is cut when it flows from the place of phlebotomy, or at the cutting of a vein, or artery: and sometimes they are made rounded according to this shape.
Chapter 47.
On the treatment of men's breasts which resemble women's breasts.
Sometimes the breasts of certain men become inflamed during their sleep (that is, when they begin to have an emission in sleep) until they resemble women's breasts: and they remain as foul apostumes.
He who therefore abhors that, should cut above the breast in a lunar section, according to this shape from line b to line g. Then scratch out all the fat. Afterwards fill the wound with incarnate medicine. Then bring together the two lips of the wound with a suture, and cure it, until it is healed.
If the breast however declines to the lower parts and becomes soft because of its size, as it happens with women: then it is necessary that two sections similar in figure to the moon be found on its two upper sides, each of which is connected to the other at both ends, until there is a greater line containing the lesser, according to this shape from line b to line g. Afterwards scratch out the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we said about sutures and powders, which is necessary for the cure, until it is healed.
If you do not close the incision of what it is necessary for you to cut, on account of the discomfort of the weak or because of the flow of blood: then it is necessary that you fill the wound with a submersed corrosive ointment, and leave it, until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then cure it, until it is healed.
Of the perforation of the apostema, which happens under the tongue.
Chapter 48.
These apostemas which happen under the tongue, are of the species of hard Strophulons, which contain cysts, and of them are those which contain humidity.
Which therefore are of those which contain humidities, it is necessary that they be cut with a lunar section, according to this form, from line b to line g, when therefore all that is in the apostema is evacuated of blood, then fill it with old oil, and leave it until another day.
Then let the plaster be removed, and let it be cured with an ointment suitable for that, until it is healed.
Which if the apostema is of the species of nodes of Strophulons, then cut over it, as we have said in the section on Strophulons equally.
If however the wound extends in this so that it emits pus, then administer to it a cauterization, according to what we have said in what has been previously mentioned.
Chapter 49.
Of the cutting of the apostema which happens on account of the Artery and Vein.
When the Artery is broken and the skin which is above it becomes consolidated, then often an apostema happens from this: and similarly it happens to the Veins also, so that an apostema and inflammation happen in them.
And the signs by which it is recognized that an apostema and inflammation are on account of the Artery and Vein, are: because, when an apostema is on account of an artery, it is long, gathered in the depth of the body: and when you press the apostema with your fingers, you feel as if there is a hissing.
And that which is on account of the Vein, is round in the obvious body.
And the cutting above this abscess is an error, and especially that which is under the armpits, and the groins, and the neck, and in many places of the body: and it is a great fault. It is necessary therefore that his treatment be managed with iron, and that which is also among them, whether it be in the extremities or in the head, it is necessary that it be managed.
Above that therefore which of them is from the inflation of the orifice of the Artery, make an incision in the skin in length. Then open the incision with forceps, afterwards the Artery: and free it from its coats, until it is exposed.
Then insert under it a needle, and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the Artery with double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of the two Arteries which are in the temples.
Then prick the place, which is between the two ligaments with a spatula, until all the blood that is in it comes out, and the abscess is resolved.
Then administer the treatment that generates pus, until the ligaments fall away: afterwards treat it with ointments suitable to it, until it is healed.
What if the abscess is on account of a cut of the Vein, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand what you can from the abscess with the skin. Then insert the needle under the place that you held with your hand, and make it penetrate: and let there be in it double thread, until you extract it from the other side. Then tie the abscess with a good ligament: according to what I said to you about the ligament of the vein, from two parts with two extremities of thread.
If however you wish to extract the thread, then insert another needle with a different thread under the whole staple at the site of the incision of the instrument: press, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then cut the staple in the middle of itself, until when what is in it comes out: then cut the excess skin, and release what has been tied from it.
Then put on it a poultice which you have submerged in wine and oil. Then administer the treatment, which is made with bandages and ointments, until it heals.
Chapter L.
Concerning the staple that happens from a twisting of the nerves.
Just as a staple occurs in the artery and vein, similarly a staple occurs in the nerves: which occurs from a blow or occurs from excessive labor and similar things: and it happens most often to those in the places of the joints, or heel, and in every place where the joints move: and it is a grave staple.
Its color resembles the rest of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain: and when it is pressed with force, one feels in it a weakness similar to numbness.
And it is not a staple collected in the depth of the body, but rather it is under the skin, and it moves to every part, and it does not proceed to the front, nor forward, nor backward to the rear.
What therefore is in the joints, does not need to be entered with iron. Perhaps a contraction occurs.
In that which of them is on the head, or on the forehead, cut the skin with a spatula. If therefore it is a small staple, then hold it with forceps, and cut it off from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and excavate it: then remove it, and close the wound with a suture: and treat it, until it heals.
Chapter 51.
On the cutting of an apostema that happens in the belly.
It happens to certain men many times in their bellies and in the rest of their bodies, thelils, which are called Fungalias, because of their resemblance to mushrooms.
Of which the root is subtle and their head is thick and their lips are inverted. And there is one of them that is small, and there is one of them that is greatly enlarged.
And I have indeed already seen a man, and in his belly there were two thelils, which were more similar to mushrooms than the others: there was no difference between them, they were white, of small root, and their lips were inverted, and they ended, and moisture flowed from them always.
I cut them therefore, and I found one to weigh about 8 and a half ounces and the other about 6 ounces. And the operation in cutting them is, that you consider then, if it is weak, humid, and the color of the thelil is white, humid, with subtle root: then cut it with a broad spatula, and let cauteria be present to you on the fire.
For often much blood is expelled during the cutting of it: prepare therefore if the blood overcomes you, then cauterize it.
Which if you see it weak, pale and timid from the cutting with iron, then take a thread made from lead and bind with it the athelul: whose method is what we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then put on the stricture of lead. Do not therefore cease to bind with lead, as many times as it impresses on the thelil, until it is cut off, and falls by itself without labor.
If however the thelil is thick of root, then in the cutting of it there is something to be feared and dreaded: especially what is in the belly.
It is possible to cut through the middle of it. Then cauterize it, so that it does not return.
Then treat it, until the wound is healed.
And beware that you do not cut into the black bile which is of a foul color, of little sensation, and of a foul appearance: for it is a cancerous abscess: and I come with a warning and a reminder of Cancer after this.
Chapter 52.
On the treatment of the elevation of the navel.
The elevation of the navel occurs from many causes. Or from a tear of the diaphragm, which is above the stomach: and there comes out of it either gut or intestine, depending on what happens in the remainder of the rupture. Or from blood that flows from a vein, or from an artery, according to what has been previously stated. Or from flatulence constricted within it.
If however it is on account of a tear of the diaphragm, and an issue of the gut: then it is a color similar to that of the body: and it is soft, without pain: and appears in different situations. And if it is on account of the protrusion of the intestine, then its situation is with what we have narrated, of a more vehement diversity. When you press it with your fingers, it is hidden: then it returns, and perhaps there is a gurgling sound: and it is greatly magnified at the entrance of the bath, and vehement labor.
If however it is on account of humidity, it is soft, then it is not hidden when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrict, nor is it added.
For if it is on account of blood, then with these signs appears an abscess turning to blackness from the tumor.
If however it is on account of flesh that has grown: then it is a serious abscess, thick, hard, and it is fixed according to one quantity.
If the swelling is due to excess flesh, then the touch of it is gentle.
And the operation regarding it is that you should consider then if the prominence of the navel is due to blood of the artery or vein or excess flesh, then it is necessary that you should abstain from its treatment. For there is fear and dread in it, as I have taught you in the chapter, in which I said that apostema occurs due to the artery and vein.
What if the prominence of the navel is due to the intestine or hernia: then it is necessary that you should instruct the weak person, so that he may hold his breath, and stand standing upright. Then mark with a branding iron around the entire navel area. Afterwards instruct him to breathe again between your hands over his back. Then apply a bandage around the navel area over the place that you marked with the branding iron. Afterwards extend the middle of the apostema upwards with a large hook. Then tie it around strongly with a thread or with a cord of firm silk binding, and let the knot of the binding be secure.
Then open the middle of the extended apostema above the bandage. If therefore you find that it has already been caught by the bandage: then pull out the secured one, and insert the index finger into it, and push the intestine towards the interior of the abdomen: and if you find a hernia, then take it with a hook, and cut away its excess.
If on the other hand the artery or vein is opposite to you: then surround it abundantly. Then return to your operation. And take two needles, and insert two strong threads into them: and insert the two needles around the area that you made around the apostema in the form of a cross, which you make penetrate.
Then tie the aposteme in four places above the needle, and if it is useful, remove the needle and leave the place until the rotten flesh falls off by itself, or cut it when it becomes subtle and rotten.
Then treat it with what is suitable from ointments, until it heals.
What if the elevation of the navel is from the thick flesh in it, or from moisture: then it is suitable to concave the aposteme, as we have said. And extract the blood, or moisture, which you find in it.
Then treat it with what consolidates the place.
Chapter 53.
On the treatment of cancer.
We have already spoken in the division of the species of cancer, and how it is the way to cure it with medicines: and to beware of it with the cure of it with iron, so that it does not become ulcerated: and we have spoken of cancer generated in the matrix, and caution in its cure.
And the ancients said that whenever cancer is in a place where its eradication is possible, such as cancer which is in the breasts or in the hip, and similar members located for extraction of all of it, especially when it is beginning and small.
When however it becomes old and is large, it is not suitable to approach it.
For I myself was not able to heal any of them: nor have I seen anyone before me who has approached that.
And the operation on it, when it is located as we have said, is to precede and dissolve the weakness with black bile several times. Then phlebotomize it if you find it with a manifest fullness.
Then prepare the weakness for preparation, in which it will be treated with operation.
Then apply to the cancer ointments that are suitable for it. Afterward press it from every part with the skin, according to the scrutation, until nothing remains of its roots: and let blood flow, and do not cut it quickly, but express the place, and wipe away all gross blood with your hand, or with any instrument that is possible there.
But if a profuse flow of blood is contrary to you from the incision of an artery or vein: then cauterize the vein, until the blood is stopped. Then treat it with the remainder of the treatment, until it is healed.
On the treatment of Dropsy.
Chapter 54. We have now explained in the division of the species of Dropsy, and how the collection of water is made: and the signs of each species, and its cure with medicines.
And that which is treated with iron, is not but the species of ascites alone: and it does not approach with iron the species of tympanitis: nor the species of hyposarca inwardly: for that is mortal.
When you have already treated this species of Dropsy, tympanitis, with medicines, and your medication has not been effective: then consider. For if debility has already befallen the weak person, or if there is another infirmity with it besides Dropsy: such as if there is with it a cough, or a loosening of the stomach, and things similar to these: then beware that you do not treat him with iron: for that is to be feared.
But if you see the weak person of overflowing strength, and there is no sickness with it besides Dropsy alone: and he is neither a child nor an old man: then the method of operation on him is, that you should lift up the weak person standing between your hands, and your assistant behind him presses out his stomach with his hand, forcing water to the lower part of the chest.
Then take a spiney spongy bone, according to this form. It has two sharp parts, is long, with a pointed extremity like the Spatula. But in it let there be something of shortness little by little, so that you do not transpierce with it during the operation to the intestine, and wound it.
Then consider. For if there is a generation of dropsy from the side of the intestines, then it is necessary that you should lengthen with the section from the navel by the quantity of three fingers, downwards directly above the chest.
If indeed the generation of dropsy is because of liver sickness, then let your section be on the left from the navel by three fingers.
And if the generation of it is because of the spleen, then let the section be on the right side: and it is not necessary also that the section be on the side above which the sick person wants to lie, so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place.
Then pierce with an instrument the whole skin. Then insert into that section, and raise your hand with the spatula between the skin, and rub, as if you are scraping it out: and let the quantity which is scraped out be the quantity of a nail, or about that.
Then scrape through, until the spatula reaches the empty place: and it is the place of water. Then extract it, and insert into the hole an instrument, whose form is this. And it is similar to a cannula: made from silver, or copper, or gold, clean and polished: which has a small hole in its lower part, and on its sides are three holes, two on one side and one on the other side: and its end is cut, according to the manner of cutting a reed, as you see: on its upper end is a handle.
When the instrument penetrates the water, then it itself descends immediately on the instrument, and thus evacuates from the water at once half the quantity.
Since if you evacuate from it more than is necessary, then perhaps the weak person dies at once through resolution of his animal spirit: or a fainting fit that approaches death befalls him.
Evacuate from it according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the weak person signify to you from the virtue of his pulse, and from his goodness.
Then withdraw the instrument, and retain the water.
Which is, that it is retained at once on account of the skin which retains the opening that is above the sifac: about which I have spoken, that you should perforate it according to that method.
Then repeat the instrument on the second day, if you see the weak person tolerate it: and withdraw also from the water a small quantity.
Do that for several days without fear, and guard yourself from error: until there does not remain from the water except a little.
If you are afraid for the weak person, and you leave a large amount from the water: then treat it with burial in hot sand, and with much sweat in bath and sun, and await its thirst: and treat it with medicines evacuative, until it is healed: and cauterize above the stomach, and liver, and spleen, after extraction of the water: according to what I have spoken in that which preceded.
On the treatment of infants who are born with their urinary places not perforated.
Chapter 45.
When any infant goes out from the womb of its mother, and the head of its bladder is not perforated, or the opening is narrow, or it is not in its proper place.
It is necessary therefore to help with the perforation of it at once when it is born with a very sharp and fine spatula, according to this method.
Then put in the hole a thin nail made of lead, and tie it: and leave it for three days, or four.
When the skin is raised to pass urine, it should be removed, and wiped. Then reduce it.
And if you do not put in the lead, it is possible that the urine which enters on the place, will not allow it to close.
He whose hole is narrow, is treated with lead, as we have said, for many days, until it is enlarged.
Those however in whom the hole is not in its proper place, are injured. That is, because among those who are born with it, the hole is at the end of the virga: wherefore she cannot urinate to the front, unless she lifts the virga with her hand upwards. And there is no generation for her, because the sperm cannot pass to the womb according to the right direction: and it is a foul and grievous disease.
And the method of operation for that is, that the weak one is placed on her back. Then extend the head of her virga with your left hand with vigorous extension, and cut the head of the head from the place of the priapus, with a needle, or a sharp spatula: as is the incision of a reed, or as you peel something, so that the middle of it comes to resemble the head of the virga: and so that the hole falls in the middle according to what is proper.
And beware for yourself during the operation of a flow of blood. For that thing has happened many times. Apply to it therefore that which stops the blood, and cure the wound, until it is healed.
On the matters concerning Albucasis which occur on the foreskin and head of the virga, and the corruption, blackness, and adhesion.
Chapter 6
These things often happen to the albather on a branch, and it is an eminence of rotten flesh.
And some of them are malignant, and some of them are not malignant.
You should therefore suspend the non-malignant one with a subtle hook, and cut it off, until you cleanse it completely. Then put on it a plaster submerged in Egyptian ointment. Then treat it after that with the dyafrincon ointment, until it is healed.
Which if the albather is malignant, of foul color, then you should administer to it a cauterization after the incision of it and its rasping.
If the albather is on the foreskin of an uncircumcised person, and part of the albather is inside the foreskin and part of it outside: then you should remove the albather that is inside first, until when it has consolidated, then treat the one outside: because when you treat them both at the same time, the foreskin does not heal unless it is perforated.
And now they also occur on the testicles and a blackening and corruption of the foreskin. You should therefore cauterize all that has already turned black, and what will decay or is already decayed.
Then apply on it after that a mixture of honey which has already been mixed with the flour of roasted grains and the crushed herbs of tritorage.
Then treat it with the remainder of the treatment, until it is healed.
If there is a flow of blood, then administer a cauterization with lunar cauterization, according to this method.
For cauterization is a remedy for two conditions at the same time, namely for a flow of blood and for an ulcer when it becomes decayed.
Which if the head of the branch is eaten away and destroyed entirely in one hour: then you should insert into the mouth of the penis a tube made of lead, so that the weakened man urinates on it.
In the adhesion of the skin to the head of the virga, and this adhesion does not occur except in one whose virga is healthy, and it is not necessary to circumcise over it: and when adhesion occurs because of a wound or apostema, it is necessary to cauterize it with a blunt spatula until the ligament is dissolved and the head of the virga is freed from every part.
What is difficult to discern with exquisite care, then it is necessary to cauterize something from the head of the virga and from the prepuce. What is, that the prepuce, when it is subtle, is perhaps perforated on account of its subtlety quickly.
Then separate the prepuce and the head of the virga with a subtle linen cloth, which has already been soaked in cold water, so that they do not adhere again.
Then let it be treated with styptic wine, until it is consolidated.
Chapter 57.
On the purification of infants, and the cure of errors that occur to them by accident.
Circumcision is not a solution of continuity, like other wounds: nevertheless since it is from our operation, our will, and its use is properly in boys, it is necessary that we indicate in this operation the better method, and the easier way leading to health.
I say therefore, that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books: since they do not use it in their laws, and it is not except what we have acquired through experimentation.
What is, that I have found the greater part of artisans and phlebotomists using purification by circumcision with a razor, and with forceps: and they use a cauterized wound, and a ligature with a thread, and an incision with a nail.
And I have already tried all these methods, and I did not find a better purification than with forceps and a ligature with a thread.
Since in cleansing with a lancet, the skin often escapes. For the skin of the prepuce has two tunics: therefore perhaps the upper skin is cut and the inner tunic remains: hence it is necessary to make an incision to cut the other, and future pain. And with the cleansing that is done by the digital method, that is, with a needle, which surgeons use, the cutting of the extremity of the member is not avoided: for perhaps it enters into its opening.
In cleansing with a nail, perhaps the iron comes out and spoils your operation: and the skin of a child is brief by nature, and often they are born in such a way that they do not need cleansing: and I have already seen it.
Cleansing with forceps and ligature with a thread has shown me a good experiment: for the forceps are proportional to the incision: therefore, because the sharpness that is above is as the sharpness that is below. When therefore you press with your hand, the two sharpnesses are proportioned, and they cut according to one operation at one time: and there is made a compression of similar figure, containing the skin of the member from all parts, with which error does not fall in any way.
And the method of operation is its own, that you cause to be extracted, especially a child, if it is one of those who understand for a little while, what you do not do, except that you bind the thread on its member only: and you let it go until another day.
Then make him rejoice and be merry in every way that is possible for you, from the fact that he receives his understanding. Then make him stand between your hands prepared in a standing position, and let him not be sitting: and hide the forceps in your sleeve or under your foot, so that the child does not see them at all, nor any of the instruments.
Then insert your hand into its branch and blow on the skin and pull it upwards until the head of the branch comes out. Then cleanse it from the filth that has accumulated in the wound.
Then tie the marked place with a double thread. Afterwards tie below it for a short space a second ligature. Then hold with your index finger, and thumb, the place of the lower ligature with good retention, and cut between the two ligatures. Then lift the skin upwards quickly, and extract the head of the branch. Then let the blood flow gradually (for it is better) and put powder on top: and over the powder a cloth in which vitellus of egg has been spread, mixed with good fresh rose oil: and let it remain on until the next day: and treat it with the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
The shape of a fork is for cleansing purposes this.
Let the two extremities be blunt and let them be cutting: so that the branch of the nail does not come out on them: and let the length of the two sharp edges be as the length of the two handles equally.
The error that occurs in cleansing is: because perhaps it escapes the inner skin entirely, or a part of it at the place of the incision.
Therefore it is necessary that you stretch it out with your nail before the marking of the place: and cut it according to equality.
What if you cannot hold it with your nail, then extract it with a hook, and cut it.
If however three days have passed and what is under the branch remains inflated, marked: then let it be until the hot apostema has settled, and excise it with ease, and cut it according to that which is prepared for you: and beware of the head of the branch. For it will not harm him.
Treatment is therefore with that which consolidates the wound from powders, which we have described in the treatise on powders: and if it cuts into the skin above the measure, and it goes to the upper parts, it will not harm him either.
Treatment is therefore with that which we have said, until it is healed.
Chapter 58.
On the extraction of retained urine from the bladder.
The retention of urine in the bladder is caused by obstruction made from stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or flesh that has grown, and similar things to these which we have spoken of as methods of treatment in the division.
And if the urine is not discharged, and you see that its retention is on account of a stone, which is already in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary that he should be made to bend over his knees. Then let his feet be placed upon his back, and let him stretch out his belly from the upper part of his back, and let him tightly constrict his breathing as much as is possible for him. The neck of the bladder is thus compressed towards the expulsion of the stone to the back, whereupon the urine is discharged.
What if it is not solved with what we have said, and the thing is vehement upon the patient: then it is necessary that you administer the extraction of it with an instrument, which is called a syringe, whose form is this: let it be of silver, and let it be subtle, thin, concave like the quill of a feather in subtlety of a radius, long in likeness to one and a half palms: to which let there be a subtle pipe at its head.
And the method of the exit of urine through it is, that you take a doubled thread, and tie at its end a wool or a cord, with a good ligature: and introduce the end of the thread into the lower part of the Syringe: and cut with forceps if anything overflows from the wool, truly introduce into the pipe with vehemence, like an Alzer.
Then anoint the siringa with oil, or with butter, and the white of an egg: and make the weak sit upon a seat, and embrocate the vessel, and its own virga with humid oils, and olive oil, and warm water.
Then insert the siringa into the virga with ease, until it reaches the root of the virga.
Then fold it over double from the part of the navel.
Then push the siringa into it, until it reaches the bladder, and the weak person feels that it has already reached the empty space: and this is not done according to this order, unless the passage, in which it goes, is where there is a tortuosity.
Then extend the thread with a wool slowly. For the catheter will follow the wool.
Then pull it out, and make the catheter run through the urine passage: and repeat the syringe, and do not cease to do that, until the bladder is emptied, and the weak person finds relief.
On the quality of cleansing the bladder with a Clyster.
Chapter 59.
When there happens to be an ulcer in the bladder, or blood congeals in it, or pus is confined in it, and one wishes to distill waters and medicines into it: then let it be done with the instrument that is called a Clyster, and this is its form.
For it is stopped, that is, closed. And in it are three holes, two on one side and one on the other side, as you see.
And the concave place, in which is that which pushes, should be according to the quantity that fills it without addition, until when it is pulled with it, something is attracted from the humidities: and when it is pushed, it expels far away: according to what makes the clyster, with which naphtha is projected, that is, Greek fire in the workshops of Mars.
When I insert the instrument to project moisture into the bladder, I introduce the extremity of the catheter into the moisture, and pull with it that which pushes upwards, for the moisture is pulled into the concavity of the catheter.
Then I introduce its extremity into the rod, according to that which we described in the syringe. Then I push the moisture with that which pushes it, for the moisture immediately reaches the bladder, so that the weak person feels it.
The shape of a thin enema instrument by which the bladder is enemad.
Let it be made from silver or gold: whose head is higher and similar to a small hook, and under that a hollow where the ligament falls.
Then take the bladder of a goat, and put in it moisture, with which instrument you will enema the bladder. Then tie it between two hollows with a strong ligature and double thread: and warm that moisture a little over the fire.
Then insert the extremity of the enema instrument into the rod, afterwards tighten your hand over the bladder with the moisture with a suitable pressure, until the weak person feels that the moisture has now reached the bladder.
If however the bladder is not present to you, then take a piece of parchment, and make from it a circle, and pierce it throughout its entire roundness. Then insert a strong thread into those holes, as they revolve. Then gather the circle, as the nest is gathered: afterwards you put in it that which you use from moistures, and oils, and waters.
Then tie it in the instrument: and do with it as you did with the bladder by expression with your hand, until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter 60.
On the extraction of a stone.
We have already spoken about the division of the species of Stone, and its cure with medicines, and I have said the difference between the Stone generated in the kidneys and bladder, and the signs of all that: and I have said the Stone in which the operation falls with the hand and incision: and there is a Stone generated in the bladder specifically: and that which is fixed on the staff: and I am narrating that with clear exposition and abbreviation.
I say therefore, that the Stone generated in the bladder, happens most often to children.
And one of its signs is that urine comes out from the bladder similar to water in its thinness: and appears in it white sand, and the weak man rubs his staff, and labors with it, and many times it hangs. Then it is erected, and goes out with that, the bottom, in many of them.
And the cure of children is easy, as long as they are up to fourteen years old. And it is difficult in the elderly. In youths, however, it is moderate, in that which is between them: and of whom the Stone is larger, the cure is easier: and if small, the care is the opposite.
When we arrive at the cure, it is necessary first to cleanse the weak person with a clyster, which will extract all the dung that is in his intestines: for it sometimes prevents the discovery of the Stone during the examination.
Then let the weak person be taken by the feet, and shaken, and moved to the lower parts: so that the Stone descends to the depth of the bladder, or jumps from a high place many times.
Then make him sit prepared between your hands, and let his hands be under his hips, so that the whole bladder is inclined downwards.
Then examine him, and feel him from the outside.
If therefore you feel a stone in the space, then apply the proper thing at once with incision upon it.
What if it does not fall under your touch altogether, then it is necessary that you wipe the index finger with oil of the left hand, if he is a weak boy: or the middle finger if he is a young man complete: and insert it into his anus, and feel for the stone, until it stands under your finger: and turn it little by little to the neck of the bladder.
Then press upon it with your finger, and push it to the exterior against the place of which you wish to make an incision: and instruct one assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct another assistant to extend the testicles with his right hand upwards: and his other hand, that he may remove the skin which is under the testicles on the part away from the place in which the incision is.
Then insert a spatula or knife with an incision, the shape of which is this. And cut in that which is between the anus and testicles, and not in the middle, to the side of the left buttock: and let the incision be above the stone, and your finger be in the anus: and let the incision be transverse, so that the exterior incision be ample, and the interior be strict, according to the quantity that it is possible for the exit of the stone from it not being larger.
Perhaps indeed the finger which is in the anus presses the stone near the incision, and it comes out without difficulty.
And know that because of the stone, in which there are angles and edges, its exit is made difficult on account of that.
And from this it is smooth, like a gland, and round: and its exit is made easy.
Therefore for those which have angles and edges, add to the incision.
What if it does not come out thus, then it is necessary that you apply above it: or tie above it with a device of the center, whose extremity is like a crescent moon, which ties above the stone and does not depart from it: or that you insert under it an instrument subtle, of curved extremity.
If you cannot exceed it, then enlarge the opening a little. What if something of blood conquers you, cut it off with a razor.
If there is a stone more than one, then first push the large one to the mouth of the bladder. Then cut on top of it. Afterwards push a small one after that, and do similarly if there are more than two.
What if the valve is very large, then it is ignorance to cut above it with a large incision. Since it happens to the weak one of two things, either that he dies, or that there is a continual dripping of urine: therefore, because the place is not consolidated at all.
Indeed administer the expulsion of it, until it goes out: or instruments on the fracture with forceps, until you extract it bit by bit.
When you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with turpentine, and aloe, and dragon's blood: and bind it, and put on it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water: so that the hot aposteme may be seated.
Then let the weak one rest on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage, until the third day. When you then loosen it, moisten the place with water, and much oil.
Then treat it with the ointment diaphenicum, and the ointment baselicum, until it is healed.
If however there occurs in the wound a hot and corrosive aposteme, and similar things: as if blood congeals in the bladder, and urine is prohibited from it: and that is recognized by the emission of blood with urine. Therefore insert your finger into the wound, and extract that blood. For if it remains, it provokes the corruption of the bladder, and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar, and water, and salt: and apply all the species with what is suitable from the treatment, until it is healed.
And it is necessary during the hours of treatment that you bind two hips, and gather, the causes of medicines which are placed on the spot.
What if the stone is small, and it is in the flesh of the virgin, and it is fixed in it, and the urine exit is blocked: then treat it with what I will narrate before you proceed to the cutting. For many times indeed you will be exempt from cutting by this treatment, for I have already tested that.
And there is, that you should take a perforator made of iron, whose form this is, triangular at the end, sharp, fixed in wood.
Then take a thread, and bind with it the branch under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then insert the iron perforator into the branch with ease, until the perforator reaches the stone itself: and turn the perforator with your hand on the stone little by little: and complete the perforation of it, until you make it penetrate from the other side.
For urine will be relieved immediately.
Then press your hand on that which remains of the stone from the outer part of the branch. For it itself breaks, and goes out with the urine, and the sick person is healed.
If however this treatment is not prepared for you, because of something that prohibits it: then bind a thread below the stone, and another thread above the stone. Then cut above the stone on the same branch between the two bindings. Then extract it. Afterwards loosen the binding, and cleanse the congealed blood which forms in the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie the thread under the stone, unless so that it does not return to the bladder: and another tie above, unless when the thread is released after the removal of the stone, the skin returns to its place, and covers the wound: and because of that it is necessary for you, when you tie the upper thread, to lift the skin upwards, so that it returns according to your complement, and covers the wound, as we have said.
Chapter 61.
Of the extraction of a stone from women.
A stone is rarely generated in women.
If however it happens to any of them a stone, then the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited because of many methods.
One of them is: that the woman is perhaps a virgin.
And the second is, that you do not find a woman who reveals herself to a physician, when she is chaste, or one of those having husbands.
The third is, that you do not find a woman well knowing this art, especially the operation with the hand.
And the fourth is the remoteness of the place of the stone: where it requires a deep incision, and in that there is fear.
What if necessity provokes to that, then it is necessary that you accept a woman physician, well knowing: and she is rarely found.
If you are deprived of them, then seek a chaste physician, subtle, and present a midwife well taught in the matter of women, or a woman who has begun to learn part of the art: make her therefore present, and command her, that she do all that you command her from the inquiry about the stone.
At first what is, to examine if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary that she insert a finger into her anus, and seek the stone.
If then he finds it, he constricts it under his finger, and then orders the midwife to insert her finger into the weak woman's vulva, and feels above the stone, after which she places her left hand on the bladder, and presses it with a good compression.
If then he finds the stone, then it is necessary that he moves it gradually from the orifice of the bladder to the lower areas with the greatest strength of his, until he reaches with it to the root of the hip.
Then he cuts above it at the opposite of the middle of the vulva at the root of the hip, from whichever side he prepares for it, and feels the stone on that side: and his finger is not removed from the stone, constricting under it: and let the incision be small at first. Then he inserts the razor above that incision.
Then he inserts the razor above that incision. If then he feels the stone, then he adds to the incision a second cut proportional in quantity to what of the stone emerges from it.
And know that there are many types of stones. For among them is the small and the large, the smooth and the rough, the long and the round having branches.
Know therefore its species, so that it may be indicated to you by this above what you are using.
If then the blood overcomes you, then apply to the place a poultice of toasted and ground, and hold it for one hour, until the bleeding stops.
Then return to your operation, until the stone emerges: and do, so that you prepare with you from the instruments, which I mentioned in the extraction of the stone from the bladder, so that you may help yourself by them in your operation.
For if the flow of blood overcomes you, and you know that the expulsion of blood is from the artery which was cut: then put powder on the place, and constrict it with decent stricturing bandages: and do not move it: and leave the stone, and do not extract it. A weak woman will perhaps die from it. Then treat the wound.
When therefore the sharpness of the blood is satiated after some days, and the place becomes putrid, then return to your operation, until the stone comes out.
Chapter 62.
On the cutting of a watery hernia.
A watery collection is not a true hernia, unless it be an aggregation of humidity in the white vascular covering that is under the skin of the testicle containing the egg: and it is named a vascular covering.
And sometimes it is in its own proper membrane, which nature has prepared for it in the part of the egg, until it becomes putrid: which is another egg, and is a skin of the testicle between the white vascular covering that we spoke of: and this does not happen except rarely.
