And the generation of this watery collection is from a weakness that happens to the testicles: for which reason this material flows out to them. And sometimes it happens from a blow on the testicles.
And this humidity has many colors. For it is either of a yellowish color, or it is a bloody red, or feculent, black, or it is a watery white, and this is the one that is most.
And the signs by which it is known where the collection of water is, are these. For if it is in the white vascular covering that we spoke of, then the swelling is round in length for a while just like the shape of an egg: and the testicle does not appear, because the humidity contains it on every side.
And if it is humidity in its own proper membrane, then the swelling is round with a part of the egg, and because of this a man thinks that it is another egg.
And if the humidity is between the skin of the testicles and the white vascular covering, then it falls under the sense.
When I apply my knowledge of the colour of humidity, then I test the colour of humidity in the apostema with the square introversion, whose shape precedes. According to that which appears in the trace of the Introversion, I judge from that which is between it.
When we proceed to a cure with iron, then it is necessary to prescribe to the weak, that they should be bled if possible for them, and you see his body full.
Then he should be placed on his back on something high and a little elevated, and many cloths should be put under him.
Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right side, who should stretch out his arm to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and to the region of the navel.
Then take a broad spatula, and cut the skin of the testicles in the middle along the length, up to near the breast; and let the incision be according to the rectitude of the equidistant line which divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white substance that comprehends; and cut out this and observe, or take care lest you cut from hence, that you cut it; and your cutting should be where it is suspended with the egg more: and subtly examine with the cutting according to the quantity that is possible for you.
Then pierce the full watery substance with a wide piercing, and extract all the water.
Then separate between the two lips of the incision with forceps, and stretch the watery substance upwards, and do not touch the skin of the testicles that comprehends; and cut the watery substance as much as it is possible for you to cut it, or with its entirety, or in a piece, especially the broad subtle part. For if you do not carefully and thoroughly examine in the incision, there will be no security, lest the water flow back.
If however the egg proceeds outward from its skin during the time of your operation: then when you have completed the incision of the womb, reduce it. Then bring together the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a suture.
Then cure it as the remaining wounds, until it is healed.
What if you find the egg corrupted by blackness of another kind, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels, which are the suspensors, fearing a flow of blood.
Then cut off the testicle with its suspensor, and extract the egg: afterwards cure it with what we have said.
If indeed water is collected in the two parts, then know that there are two pipes: therefore cut the other part equally according to what you have done in the other.
And if it is equal to you, that there be one operation, then do it: afterwards wipe away the blood. And insert into the incisions a thread soaked in oil, or in rose oil: and put on the dressing a thread which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over the two testicles, and the navel: and put above double cloths, and they are poultices: and tie them above with a bandage, which has six according to this form.
Then let two cloths be taken, and they be sewn, and filled with medicated thread, according to this likeness: and let the extremities be made which are pressed from a cot, or a wet thread: and let them be tied with a bandage in the groin of the arms: and one extremity let it reach above the thigh up to the back, and the second let it reach to the part of the breast: and two extremities above the two hips below, and two other extremities above the two groins, and all the bandage be tied in the groin of the arms.
And when this ramex is treated artificially with a cautery at the place of the section with iron; and it is, that you take a sharp cautery knife, and cut the skin of the testicles; and it is ignited, according to what we have narrated: until when there appears a white scab containing water: then take the cautery, according to this form.
The Greek letters are absorbed.
Then puncture that scab with it, and it is ignited, until all moisture comes out.
Then stretch the scab with forceps, and scrape it with a sharp ignited cautery, and cut it according to what is possible for you, until you eradicate the whole of it.
And beware lest the fire touch it.
And know that this operation is safer, and less inclined to a flow of blood, and better than the operation with a section.
If indeed an adverse condition makes itself known to you at the time of the section, or at the time of the cautery, whether it be a hot aposteme, or a flow of blood, or something else: then it is necessary that you treat that which makes the adverse condition known to you from that with a cure which is suitable for it, according to what has been previously stated.
If however he is weak and timid, and does not look forward to this operation, because of its horror: then administer the puncture according to what I have narrated it to be.
When it is confirmed to you by that which we have spoken of concerning the signs, that the ramex is watery: then it is necessary that you make the weak person sit on an elevated seat.
Then puncture the aposteme in its lower part with a broad spatula: and put the puncture according to the length of the body, and let it be wide open, until all the water runs out.
Then put a dressing on the place of the cut, and bind it, and let it stay so that the remainder of the water runs out: then treat it, until the wound is healed.
If however the blockage is an obstacle to the exit of water at the time when you perforate it: and it is not except on account of that, because the white membrane makes a blockage in the opening of the wound, and prohibits the exit of water: then it is necessary that you insert a feather into the wound, or an instrument with which water of dropsy is extracted, whose form has preceded: or add for a short time in the operation of the wound.
And you should know that the water returns and accumulates after six months, or around that time. When therefore it accumulates, then it should be tapped according to the same method, and the weak days will pass.
Chapter 63.
On the treatment of a fleshy ulcer.
You should know that in the incision above this ulcer, there is a fear of inducing destruction in many conditions. Wherefore it seems to me that its neglect is beneficial for its healing.
And I recall the operation on it, and the appearance of an apostema.
I say therefore, that many gatherings occur in the bodies, from which the testicles are composed: and this happens for many reasons.
Or from an excess of sharp or acidic humor, which flows to the testicles. Or from a blow.
And the color of the gathering is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a serious gathering.
And perhaps it is a stone-like gathering, whose color is dark, and there is no sensation in it.
And sometimes it happens from the knotting of the arteries, and their swelling: as I have already mentioned before: or from the swelling of the veins.
That which is therefore from the swelling of the arteries, is recognized by the condition of the gathering, when you press it with your fingers. And it is not proper to touch it directly.
That which is made from the inflation of veins is not dispersed from it by compression with the fingers.
And now it is possible that a section on this species is made and on the rest of the flesh and it is as one cuts the skin of the testicles. Then extend the egg upwards, and extract it with the white siftach: and free the suspensor from the vessels, and tie up the vessels: and cut the suspensor after you have freed it from every part of the parts of the egg.
If then the egg is consolidated with those born flesh, then it is proper that you should pull the egg and cut it.
And if an adhesion is between any of the siphacet or in that which is between the vessels: then it is proper that you free the whole of that adhesion, and cut it with a round incision.
If however there is a nativity of flesh in the place of adhesion which is behind: then it is proper that you cut the whole of it, and extract the egg, as we have said.
When therefore your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool infused in rose oil and wine: afterwards cure it with the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
Chapter 64.
On the treatment of Varices, which is with Veins.
Uitis is an unresolved aposteme, which occurs with a certain wrapping, similar to a boil, with softening of the testicles: and it makes difficult movement and exercise on the infirm, and walking.
And in the cure of this sickness is fear, because of that which has preceded it, the memory remains.
It is true that we should say the operation on it according to what the first ones did.
I say therefore, that it is proper to make the infirm person sit on an elevated seat. Then strike the suspension of the testicles to the lower parts. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, with the instruments that are nearest to the rod: and let another servant hold them, and let him stretch them with a vigorous stretching.
Then cut with a broad sharp spatula a transverse section in the direction of the vessels, until the vessels are exposed.
Then scratch away from every part, as we have told you in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
Afterwards fix in them a needle in which is a double thread, and tie it in the first places to which the ties occur: and tie it again at the last of them. Then cut it in a straight section according to the length of the body, and extract what is gathered from foul corrupted humors.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which it is customary to generate a sanative, so that the vessels which nourish one of the testicles fall. For it is not an evil through that.
If however the vessel occurs to all the vessels, then it is necessary that the testicles with the vessels be extracted for this: so that the ovum is not deprived of nourishment, on account of the incision, and wither, or dry up, and is not a help with them.
Chapter 65.
Of the treatment of Intestinal hernias.
The coming out of this hernia is from a section, which occurs in the siphac extended above the navel on the groin side from the middle of the navel.
Why the intestines come down from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the siphac or from its extension.
And these two kinds occur from many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a shout, or the lifting of a heavy thing, and similar things.
And the sign is when it is from the extension of the wrist. It is what happens gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly: and it is an abscess equal in depth to the intestine: therefore, because the wrist compresses the intestine.
And its sign is when it is from a section of the wrist, because it causes sudden violent pain from the beginning: and it is a diverse abscess appearing under the skin nearby: and that is because of the exit of the intestine, and its course to the outside of the wrist.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine a hernia: and this is called intestinal Ramex and hernia: and sometimes it happens with bloating.
And sometimes feces runs into the intestine and is retained there: and it is with that a danger of weakness: because it causes severe pain, especially when it is pressed.
And in the cure of this kind of illness with iron there is fear: for which it is necessary to beware of the case in it.
And the method of the operation is, that you should order the weak person, to reduce the intestine with his hand to the interior of its own concavity, if it has fallen back. Then he should be lifted up onto his neck between your hands: and lift up his thighs.
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin to the upper parts, and cut the skin of the testicles along its entire length. Then fix on both lips of the incision hooks, according to which you will indicate for opening the incision with them: and let the incision be according to the quantity that is possible, so that the egg can come out from it.
Then scratch the wrist, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until when the white wrist is detected, hard on every side: then insert your index finger into that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white wrist, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the wrist according to, and release with it the adhesion that is in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move with your right hand to the interior of the cut of the testicles: and with this extend the white sifach upwards, with your left hand: and lift the mouth with the sifach to the place of the incision: and instruct the assistant, that he should extend the mouth upwards: and you loosen the adhesion, which is behind the completed solution.
And search with your fingers, that there should not be anything there from the intestine entwined in the white and hard sifach. If you find something of it: then push it to the lower belly.
Then take a needle, in which is a thick thread, made a ligature from ten threads: and introduce it at the end of the sifach, that is, of the tunic, which is under the skin of the testicles that follows the incision: then cut the ends that project from the thread, until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over others with a figure that is in the form of a cross: and tie with them the sifach, of which we spoke, which is under the skin of the testicles with a vehement ligature, until it cannot allow any of the vessels, which nourish them to send to them anything: so that there does not occur from it a hot apostema. And put again a second ligature outside the first ligature, a distance of less than two fingers from it. And after these two ligatures, let out from the sifach, which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity of the size of a finger: and cut the rest entirely according to its roundness, and remove the mouth from it.
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles at the incision, from which runs blood and serum: as we have narrated in what was previously said.
Then administer a wool submerged in oil, and put it on the wound: and administer the ligature that we have narrated. And when the white vitriarized sifach which we mentioned is cauterized, after its incision, fearing a flow of blood. For this often happens. And release the ligament, until it falls by itself.
If its fall is delayed, then let it be bathed with warm water: and put on top of it what we mentioned, until it falls.
Then treat the wound with the remainder of the treatment of wounds, until it is cured.

Concerning the Vein that has a wart.
On this vein I have not seen anyone who dared to perform its cure with iron.

Chapter 67.
Concerning the rupture that occurs in the groins.
When a rupture occurs in the groins, as we said, and the place protrudes, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is little, and returns every hour: but truly if the time with this condition is prolonged, a fissure is added in the sifach, until the intestines descend into the sifach.
And this happens from the extension of the sifach which is in the groins, as we said. Which is because the sifach extends: then becomes soft, and the place becomes calloused, and protrudes.
And its treatment is with a cauterization, as was previously explained.
And sometimes it is treated with iron, in this manner: and it is that the weak person lies on his back between your hands. Then cut the place of the rupture and the prominent part, a cross-section in width, according to the quantity of three fingers.
Then stretch the Alsifak and what is under the skin until when it is detected the white Sifach which is under the skin that follows it.
Then take a rasp and put it on the prominent place of the Sifach and press it to the depth of the belly.
Then sew two prominent places on the extremity of the rasp from the Sifach and join one of them with the other: then extract the extremity of the rasp.
And do not cut the Alsifak at all, nor stretch the groin, nor anything else, as I have made you know in the treatment of intestinal rupture.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds. When you cut the threads, clean it and restore the wound, until it becomes consolidated.
For the Sifach is contracted, and prominence of the rupture is not added.
And cauterization is better in this place: since it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles often becomes softened in certain men, because of which the flesh that is between them becomes softened and its appearance becomes foul.
Therefore it is necessary for him who is asked to cure it, to make the weak one lie on his back, and to cut the entire skin that has been softened above the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if necessary, first remove the excess of the softened skin with three or four sutures, and secure the suture.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it with the treatment of other wounds, until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
Chapter 69.
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden by our law, and because of that it would be permissible for me not to mention it in my book, and its mention is not necessary except for two reasons.
One of which is that it be in the science of medicine when he is questioned about it, and so that he knows the cure for one to whom it happens.
And the other method is that we often need to castrate certain animals for our utility through them, such as mules, boars, and cats, and similar ones among animals.
I say therefore, that castration is done in two ways. Or by extraction. Or by splitting and cutting.
In that which is done by extraction, the method of operation is: that we make the animal sit in hot water, until its testicles soften and relax, and hang down: then we extract them with our hand, until they dissolve and do not appear to the touch.
In castration by splitting and cutting, it is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the spermatic cord, and cut above all one ovum with a single section, until when two ovum proceed: then cut what is after you have excised both, and do not leave on them any of the sifaket except subtle sifac, which is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that which is done by extraction: because extraction perhaps leaves something of the testicles, for which reason the animal desires coitus.
Then treat the wound, until it heals.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of the hermaphrodite of two methods.
Hermaphrodite from urine is a second two modes. A wound of theirs is, which appears in what follows the space, or on the skin of the testicles, in what is between the two testicles, a figure like a woman's vulva, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine runs from what is on the skin of the testicles.
In women however is one species, and is the woman's vulva above the pubes as the testicles of a small man entirely, protruding to the outside: of which one is like the penis of a man, and two like two testicles.
And the treatment of the three species, two from men, and one species from women, is: that it is necessary to cut away the added flesh, until the impression of them disappears. Then treat them with the cure of remaining wounds.
In the second species of men, from which urine exits, which is on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all.
Chapter 71.
Concerning the cutting of the tent-like thing, and the flesh that protrudes in the vulvas of women.
The prepuce perhaps is added over the natural thing, until it becomes foul and its appearance is ugly: and sometimes it becomes magnified in some women to such a degree, that it expands like in men, and reaches up to the coitus.
It is necessary therefore to hold the excess of the prepuce with the hand, or with a hook, and cut it: and do not go too deep in the cutting, especially at the root, so that there does not occur a flow of blood.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds, until it heals.
The flesh that arises is the flesh that is born in the opening of the womb, until it fills it: and perhaps it protrudes to the outside like a tail: and because of this some of the first call the disease "caudate". It is necessary therefore that we incise it as we incise the tentskin and treat it until it is healed.
Of the treatment of Alratica, which is a woman's ulcer not having been perforated.
Chapter 72.
Alratica is, that it is a woman's ulcer not perforated, or is a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is from a disease which preceded it: and this itself comes either from flesh born added, or from sifach subtle, or from a spatula: and it comes either in the depth of the matrix, or in its sides, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part of it: and prohibits coitus and impregnation, and childbirth, and perhaps prohibits menstruation.
And its recognition is made by the appearance of an obstetrician, if the obstruction is apparent nearby.
If however it is not apparent, then feel for it with your fingers, or with a probe.
If however the obstruction is from subtle sifach, and it is near to both lips: then touch it and break it apart.
And it is, that you put upon the two lips a poultice.
Then place your indexes of both hands together, and let the woman be on her back with her thighs spread apart. Then stretch out the two lips with force, until the subtle sifach is broken apart, and the obstruction is opened.
Then take a woolen thread, and dip it in oil, and put it on the place: and let the woman apply it every day, so that the place is not consolidated by another thing.
If however the sifach is thick and dense: then it is necessary to cut it out with a broad spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
If however the obstruction is from flesh born, then suspend it with hooks, and incise it: and let there be with you medicines which sedate the flow of blood without biting, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and thus mixed with the whites of eggs.
Then administer a wide tube made of lead, so that the wound does not heal quickly, and it holds for some days: and administer a bandage made from dry linen, then the rest will be cured by treatment, until it is healed.
And when there arises in the matrix a nativity of other flesh: it is necessary therefore that they be cut according to this method: for there is not an apostema which is cancerous, for an apostema is cancerous which is in the matrix, nor does it become contrary with iron at all.
Chapter 73.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, of Athehelil, and of the redness of the buttocks in women's wounds.
Hemorrhoids indeed are the openings of the veins, until from them flows much blood continually.
When therefore hemorrhoids become chronic, they become thelil: and I have already spoken of the division of their species, and their signs: and I will say here which of them receive treatment, and which not.
I say therefore, that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the matrix, and do not appear to the senses: then there is no treatment for them with iron.
But those of them which are in the opening of the matrix, upon which the sensation falls, are those which can be treated.
It is necessary therefore that you send the woman into a cold house. Then extend the hemorrhoids with the forks, or with rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle over them at the flow of blood from one powder of incisions without biting: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and incense, and similar to them.
Then press her feet against the wall for one hour. Afterwards put her into cold water.
For if the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and crushed pomegranates, and gall, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it over its back.
If therefore blood is drawn with it, it is good: and if not, make blisters adhere to the back and the breasts, without scarification.
Then take wool and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of arnoglossa, or the juice of the branches of aulalat, that is, aglanter, Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the place.
When therefore the aposteme has rested, then treat the place with ointments, until it is healed.
The Albarth root is similar to the heads of alhaasse, and its appearance is rough.
It is necessary therefore that you cut what appears from it, according to what I said equally in the treatment of ailments: and treat it, until it is healed.
Chapter 23.
Of the perforation of the uterus which occurs in the matrix.
There occur in the matrix many kinds of apostemes, such as cancer, and the aposteme of stones, and ulcers, and adubelati, and alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and ragadiae, and thelil, and hot aposteme.
And I have already spoken of all these diseases and their kinds, and the signs of them, and their cures in the division: it is necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot aposteme which occurs in the matrix, when it is among the apostemes which collect pus, and you should know how its opening is made with iron.
It is necessary therefore that you consider. Then if the pain of the aposteme in its beginning is acute with percussion and inflammation and fever: and you see it to be red: if sense falls upon it, then do not hasten with its perforation: and treat it with that which helps against maturation, until when the acuteness of the accidents has rested.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a seat that has two seats, and she should lean back or lie on her back, and bring her feet to the lower part of her abdomen: and her hips should be expanded, and she should put her arms under her thighs, and tie both with a ligature close to that.
Then the midwife should sit on the right side, and administer the instrument by which the orifice of the matrix is opened.
And it is necessary when you administer this instrument, that you fix with the radius the depth of the woman's matrix: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and harms the weak.
If the instrument is more than the depth, then it is necessary that you put pillows on the surface of the depth of the matrix: so that the entrance of the whole instrument into the depth of the matrix is prohibited: and it is necessary that the midwife puts a thread which runs in the instrument, from the upper side: and that she holds the instrument, and that the servant turns the thread, until the depth of the matrix is opened.
When therefore the exit appears, and is touched by the hand, and is soft and mild: then it is necessary that you cut it at its head with a broad spatula.
When therefore the sanies are evacuated, then it is necessary that you put on the wound a bandage submerged in rose oil: or green oil, in which there is some astringency: and put on the bandage, and extract the section from the depth of the matrix.
And put outside on the matrix, and on the pubes clean wool submerged in water, in which mallows have been boiled.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it, until it heals.
And when the matrix and wound are washed, it is cleansed with water and honey: then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled: then anoint with ointment.
What if the wound is hidden within the matrix, then it is necessary to prohibit the cure of it with iron, but rather to cure it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter 70.
The doctrine of obstetrics, how they medicate living embryos, according to an unnatural birth figure.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the figure of a natural birth.
From the signs of it are, that when you see a woman pressed at the lower parts, and desires to smell the air, and is alleviated above what is above her from the birth, and there is a hastening of the exit of the embryo: then know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and its exit is over its head, and the afterbirth with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary to press her womb, so that the embryo may come down quickly.
For when it descends over its head, the afterbirth descends with it, and is cleansed from those superfluities of a good cleansing.
But that which is besides this birth, is unnatural, unpraiseworthy.
For when the fetus comes out over its feet, and its body comes out before its head, and its feet, and one of its hands, or one of its feet: or its head and its hands come out: or its belly comes out: and perhaps it is inverted over its neck, and similar things from unpraiseworthy figures.
It is necessary therefore for the obstetrician to be prudent, subtle in all these things, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing every figure of them, and how the device is in it, and is signified by that, and is established upon it.
When the fetus moves up above its head with its natural exit and presses upon the woman, and parturition becomes difficult for her, and you see her strength is already weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or let women hold her; and fumigate her vulva with a decoction of fenugreek, and with humid oils.
Then the midwife should insert her little spatula between her fingers and find the secondine with it and cut it with her nail until what is in it runs out from the humidity; and press the woman's abdomen until the fetus comes down.
If it does not come down, then it is necessary that the woman be given a clyster made from fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil.
Then order her after the clyster to be compressed: and make her sneeze with a concoction, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
If both hands of the fetus come out first, then it is necessary that you push them back with ease, little by little. If it does not pass into the birth passage, then put the woman on a seat and lift her feet up; then strike the seat against the ground; and let the woman be held, so that she does not fall with the striking.
If the hands do not come out and the fetus dies: then cut them off, and extract the remainder of the fetus; and tie its hand with cloth, and pull it out gently: for it will come out.
The embryo comes out over its feet. When the fetus comes out over its feet, then it is necessary to push them upwards; then turn the fetus little by little; afterwards pull it out evenly.
Then take one of its feet and stretch it out little by little.
When the suppurating matter comes out up to the hips, then order him to be compressed and make him sneeze with the confection, for it will come out, if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have described, then reduce the fomentation little by little, until you put him according to his natural shape. For it will come out then with an easy exit.
What if it is prohibited with all that we have described, then take from the mucus of the altea, and the oil of sesame, and the dissolved gum, and strike everything in a mortar with a good stroke, then smear the ulcer of the woman and her lower abdomen. Then make her sit in warm water, until she gets the hypogastric region affected.
When you see that her lower parts are already warmed, then make for her a seat of myrrh and apply it. When she has held the seat for one hour, then make her sit on the seat. Then make her sneeze and constrict its mouth and nose, and press the lower part of the abdomen with an easy compression. For the pus will come out immediately.
The fetus comes out over the knees and hands. When it comes out according to this form, then insert his hands gradually into the introitus. Then the woman will be raised over her neck, and her feet will hang down to the lower parts, and she herself will sit reclining on a bed, and will clasp her hands. Then press above her abdomen gradually. Then extract what is under her feet from the pubic area, until it is prepared in the lower part. What if the fetus does not come out, then take her feet and move them with a vigorous motion. Then press what is above the pubic area gently, until the fetus rises to the upper parts. Then he should insert his hands, and gently straighten the fetus: and order the woman to compress, until the fetus comes out.
The fetus comes out hanging sideways from the hands. It is brought down in the reduction of his hands. If however he cannot reduce it, then he should elevate the woman, and make her walk.
If indeed she cannot walk, then he should make her lie on a bed: and strike her thighs with a vigorous shaking.
Then administer the ointment that you prepared from mucilages.
Which if the part taken accepts it, then make her sit on a seat. Then attend to the reduction with his hands, and straighten the fetus according to its natural figure: and make the woman sneeze, and order her to compress herself, until it comes out.
The fetus emerges over its shoulder, with hands outstretched, and its face is towards the back of its mother. It is necessary that the midwife holds the hand of the fetus, then she should turn it around gently, and straighten it with ease.
When it is straightened, then put on its neck what we have prepared from oil and mucilages.
Then order her to move it gently. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and order her to lean to the right side. Then order her to compress herself: and make her sneeze with violence.
The prepared fetus comes out over the flank. When it descends to the opening of the womb in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail, until it is evacuated from moisture.
If I suspend it above the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel, so that it is not retained and dies.
Then push the fetus to the inside, until you place it according to what is appropriate, and tell the woman to press herself several times, for it will come out with a light exit.
The exit of twins, or of many fetuses. Know that twins often are born, and sometimes three, and four. But truly that is extraordinary, and rarely happens.
Five is a thing beyond nature, and they do not live fully: and the afterbirth contains them, however many they are, as one secundine: and they are separated by a siphach, distinguishing between them a tied ligament at the navel of each of them.
And sometimes they come out just as one fetus comes out with a natural and easy delivery, and they come out with an infamous delivery, as we have described.
What if some of them are difficult at birth, and they reach that which we spoke of, concerning unnatural positions, then treat them as we have described: and let it be with subtle skill, and do what is done with ease and slowness, and be ingenious according to every figure with what is prepared for him from the guiding ingenuity towards health.
A recollection of what is formed in the womb from embryos, and are aborted.
Sometimes one is formed in the womb, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten: and it has been verified by me, that a woman aborting has expelled seven, and another fifteen, all formed.
Which was done for the measurement of the glorious wise one.
This therefore is all that is necessary to be in the science of Midwifery. For a hole will penetrate to something similar to that: he should apply to it with what is suitable.
Chapter 76, Head or Chapter Seventy-Six
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I have said in the division of medication, and it does not come out, and you need to use an operation with the hand, then it is necessary that you consider.
If the woman is of healthy strength and does not have any of the accidents for which loss is feared over her, then it is necessary that the woman should be placed on a bed, on her back, and her head should be bent downwards, and her thighs lifted up: and a servant should hold her from both sides, or she should be tied to the bed, so that her body does not extrude during the extraction of the fetus.
Then the mouth of the matrix should be moistened with humid oils, with mucus of the altea plant, and fenugreek, and linseed.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucus: then she should insert it into the matrix with ease. Then she should seek with it the place where the nails are fixed from the fetus, and the places suitable for that.
Consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend on its head: then fix the hooks in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its armpit, or in the places near the ribs, and under the hypochondria.
If however it has descended on its feet, then in its breast, and its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand, and put its curve in what is between the fingers of the left hand: and insert with the hand with ease, and fix the hook in one of those places which we have spoken of, until it reaches the empty space.
Then he should insert on the opposite side another hook or a third, if necessary, so that the contraction is equal and does not lean to one side.
Then it should be extended with an equal extension, and the extension is not just according to straightness, but rather it should be moved to every side, so that the exit of it is alleviated, as happens with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is fitting for what is between them, that the extension should be made gentle. If a part of it is retained, then the midwife should anoint some fingers with oil and insert them from the side, so that she turns it out with them, what is retained.
If a part of the fetus comes out, then the hooks should be moved to another place that is higher: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If then a hand comes out before the other, and it is not possible to push it back, because of its constriction: then it is necessary that a cloth be wrapped over it. Then pull it out until when the whole comes out, cut it at the joint of the arm, or at the elbow: and thus it is necessary that you do the same with the other hand, and with the two feet.
If the head of the fetus is large, or there is a constriction at the exit, or there is water collected on its head: then it is necessary that a sharp Spatumile be inserted between the fingers, and that with it the head should be grasped, and the water extracted: or it should be broken with an instrument called Almisdac: whose form comes with the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows.
Similarly, he should do if the fetus is of a large-headed nature, then it is necessary that the shoulder be cut: or it should be extracted with a misdach, as we have said. Then grasp the bones with forceps.
What if the head protrudes and is constricted at the fork then it will be found until the humidity that is in the chest is poured out.
If however it does not become complicated and nor does it press on for the exit: then cut the head bit by bit, according to what is possible for you.
What if the lower part of the belly is an accumulation or there is dropsy in it: then it is necessary that you perforate it, until humidity runs out from it.
If indeed the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction to the mouth of the matrix is light.
If however it is constricted at the belly or chest: then it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth which you have wrapped over your hand: and find the belly or chest, until what is in them runs out.
If however the remaining limbs are delivered and the head returns: then the Midwife should insert her left hand. If indeed the mouth of the matrix is open, then she should insert her hand into the depth of the matrix, and seek with it the head, and draw it with her fingers to the mouth of the matrix: then she should insert in it one hook, or two hooks, and draw it with them.
What if the mouth of the matrix is constricted, on account of the hot apostema which has happened to it: then it is not necessary that she should labor over it, but rather it is necessary to administer an effusion of humid things, and ointments: and administer plasters: and sit in waters which soften and moisten.
What if the fetus is on its side, then it is possible that it will come out evenly: then administer what we have said regarding a living fetus.
What if it is not possible, then cut bit by bit, and extract.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything of the afterbirth inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we have said regarding hot apostumes which occur in the matrices.
What if there occurs a flow of blood, then let it be stopped with astringent waters, and administer the remainder of the cure.
And I have indeed already seen a woman, in whose womb a dead fetus was, then she became pregnant on top of it with another, afterwards the other fetus also died. Therefore, a postule occurred to her after a long time on her navel, and it became inflated, until it was opened: and it began to emit pus.
I was called therefore to her cure, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound was not consolidated.
I put therefore on it certain strong attractant plasters: and the bone came out from its place. Then several days passed for her, and another bone came out. I was astonished therefore at that, since there is no bone in the womb.
I thought therefore, that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I examined the wound, and I extracted many bones, with the woman being in her best condition: and she lived for a long time afterwards, and a small amount of pus came out from the place.
And I did not confirm this extraordinary thing, except that there is science and assistance in it, for what the medical artisan administers with his hand from the cure.
Chapter 78.
On the forms of necessary instruments for extracting the fetus.
The shape of the Vertiginis by which the matrix is opened.
This figure below is the form of a Strictor, which has equal books, and on which are two equal vertiges at the extremities of two wooden pieces. Truly this Vertige ought to be finer than the Strictor, and that it should be made either from ebony or boxwood.
The width of each piece of wood is about two fingers, and the thickness of each one is about one finger, and the length of each one is a palm and a half; and in the middle of the two pieces of wood there are two additions made from the same type of wood, which have already been fixed to both, whose length is more than half a palm, and the width of each one is about two fingers or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, so that it opens with them when you turn the two vertigines.
Another form similar to that one, more subtle and lighter.
Let it be made from ebony wood or boxwood, according to the likeness of the forceps. However, on the extremity of it there are two additions, as you see here above: and the length of each addition is about a palm, and the width of each one is two fingers.
When you want to open the matrix with it, then make a woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging, what is between her thighs open. Then insert these two joined additions into the matrix, and you hold the end of the instrument below between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity that you want from the opening of the mouth of the matrix, until the midwife does what she wants.
The shape of another Vertiginis which the ancients called the shape of the Impeller by which the fetus is pushed out.
The shape of the Almisdac, with which the large head is pressed, and it is similar to the forceps, which has teeth at the extremity, as you see.
And sometimes it is made with a wrapping, like forceps according to this shape, as you see, which has teeth like the teeth of a saw, by which it cuts and presses.
The shape of a bandage having one spike.
The shape of a bandage having two spikes.
The shape of scissors having two extremities for cutting off the head.
The shape of two broad scissors.
All these instruments are exercised, and the more their kinds are multiplied, and the more they are prepared by the artisan, the swifter he is at his operation, and the higher he is among men, on account of their quantity.
Do not therefore despise any of them, so that it may be prepared by you. Their necessity is indeed inexcusable.
Chapter 78.
On the extraction of the afterbirth.
When the afterbirth is retained with the part, then it is necessary that you should order the weak one to retain its breath. Then make her sneeze with a condiment: and bind your hand over her mouth, and nostrils. If it then comes out by this means, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and pierce in the cover a hole: and put in it expelling herbs of the matrix, such as calamint, rue, and dill, and chamomile, and sesame, and lignous cassia, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them with water, and put them over the fire.
Then put a bundle of reeds over the hole of the cover of the pot, and another extremity into the mouth of the matrix: and let her hold it until the vapour penetrates to the concavity of the matrix.
Then make it sneeze, as we have said. For the second one will come out with ease.
If however it remains after this treatment, and does not come out: then instruct the Midwife to immerse her hand in sesame oil or flaxseed oil. Then let her insert into the womb, and search for it with that the second one. When therefore she has found it, then let her take it, and pull it out little by little.
If however it is attached deep in the womb, then let her insert her hand, according to what we have described, until when she finds the second one, and pulls it out little by little according to what is proper, so that the womb does not fall during violent pulling: indeed it is necessary, that it be turned with ease to the right and left sides: then let there be added to the amount of the pulling. It itself will cut then, and will be separated, and will come out from the adhering.
Which if the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already described: treat it with sneezing, and from a medication of an ointment with herbs.
If however it does not come out with all that we have described, then beware that you do not fatigue yourself over it in repeated attempts at extraction.
It is necessary indeed, that what comes out to the mouth of the womb from it, be tied to the thigh of the woman. Then anoint her with the ointment called tetrapharmacon. For it will putrefy it after some days, and dissolve it, and bring it out.
Truly however when it putrefies, a bad smell rises from it to the stomach and head, and harms the weak woman. It is necessary therefore that fumigations suitable for it be administered.
Certain of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of nasturtium and fig and sycamore.
The form of an instrument with which a woman is fumigated for the retention of the secundina and menses.
Let a bowl be made similar to an alcama or from clay: and let the wide end be placed over the fire: and let the fumigation be put on the coals: let her hold it, until that fumigation is consumed: and let another be repeated.
Chapter 79.
On the cure of an unperforated anus.
Many of the boys are born, and their anus is not perforated, whom a subtle fistula has already closed. It is necessary therefore, that the midwife should perforate that fistula with her finger: and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp spatula: and let her beware of the arm, lest she touch it.
Then put on top of it a woolen cloth soaked in wine and oil. Then cure it with ointments, until it is healed.
But if you fear that it will close, then put a lead pipe in the opening for many days, and let it be removed when the boy wants to defecate.
And now the closure of the anus has also occurred from the consolidation of a wound or an abscess. It is necessary therefore that the consolidation be cut, then cured with what we have said about the cure and lead.
Chapter 80.
On the cure of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
The fistulas that occur in the lower parts are a knot and a thickness that occur near the anus of the fundament or in the space of one of the parts: and it is one fistula or several.
When therefore that knot becomes old, it opens, and a watery white humidity or subtle pus runs out from it.
And when there are some of these fistulas that penetrate. Therefore the penetrating ones are recognized by that which comes out of the evacuation and by the flatulence when the weak one uses the evacuation and perhaps comes out of the worms.
And there are among them fistulas when they are in a space penetrating up to the bladder and up to the passage of the virga. And there are among them penetrating ones up to the joint of the hip and up to the knot of the tail.
From that by which the penetrating fistula is recognized up to the anus, also from the non-penetrating one, it is that you insert your index finger into the anus and you insert a subtle probe made of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuousness.
That if there is tortuousness in it, then insert into it a subtle probe made of lead or a hair from the hairs of horses, until you feel the probe or the hair on your finger.
That if you do not feel it deeply, nor does anything come out of the opening from the evacuation, nor flatulence, nor worms as I have said, then know that it is a non-penetrating one: proceed therefore to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating up to the bladder or to the passage of urine, then its signification is the exit of urine from it, and its prohibition from this that the place be consolidated with medicines.
If it is penetrating up to the joint of the hip or to the socket of the hip, then its sign is that the probe penetrates up to that place, if there is no tortuousness up to the mouth: and the finding of pain in the surrounding area of the part, and that pus always comes out of it: and that medication is not effective in it, nor is it consolidated with an ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity to him, from foolish medicines, on which a form is formed.
In that which is not penetrating and not chronic, healing is expected with a plaster: according to what I tell you, and I have already proven: and it is, so that the weak person lies on their back under your hands: and lift their legs up above their hips, and their hips are inclined towards their belly. Then a probe of lead or copper is inserted, if there is a tortuousness in the fistula, until you know where the probe passes through.
If the weak person feels it around their anus, then it is necessary that you insert your index finger into the anus.
If you feel on your finger that the probe has already penetrated through and detected, besides what you feel between your finger and the siphac or flesh: then you certainly know that it is penetrating: do not therefore labor in it, since its healing is not, as we have said.
They have said, however, that a callus is healed in certain men and from the medication which they hope for a remedy, it is to apply a subtle cauterium of ignes according to the width of the fistula, as previously described, and insert the ignited thing into the fistula, until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that two or three times, until you know that all those added fleshy growths which are similar to the filter of a bird's pen have already been seared.
Then treat it with linen wraps in butter, until the seared growths come out: then treat it with ointments that generate and consolidate flesh.
If it is healed, it is good.
And if not, then it is not healed with any other cure.
And if the probe comes out and does not reach to your finger which is in the anus, and there is between it and the probe a thick covering of flesh or siphac: and you see the fistula in what follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you will dissect with the probe that is in the fistula, until the dissection reaches where the probe's extremity reaches, and the probe is freed and falls out.
Then clean those filtered flesh parts that resemble the tubes of a bird's feather, so that nothing remains of them.
But if the blood overcomes you, and it separates between you and your operation so that it cuts off those flesh parts: then what is done is better and for a speedier healing, to cauterize it with fire, or with sharp medicine.
For the cauterization with fire brings together good habits, an attachment of those flesh parts, and a cutting off of blood, and a drying of humidities.
Then treat it with bandages wrapped in butter, or pounded grasses, until the place emits pus, and those attached flesh parts go out into the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments, that generate hard flesh: and there are medicines in which there are astringents and drying.
For when it is restored, then already it is healed: and do not repeat the treatment.
But if the fistula has already penetrated to the depth of the anus, and is prolonged from the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus, and examine with it.
If therefore you feel a thinness, and between you and it there is a covering of sifac or flesh, and it is near to the penetration: then there is no operation on that, except according to the way of confidence and hope.
Which is, that one of the three methods is administered in it: either you cauterize it, as we have said: or you cut it, until you obtain its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert bandages, and a cure from nearby. And do not proceed far with the cutting, so that you do not injure the continence of the anus, and it happens over the weak point of the exit of the bowel without control. Then treat it with what we have said.
For a strong [wound] will be healed: either you will lengthen the dressing or clean it after you cut it close to the bone, as we have said, or with a probe, or with another instrument of a sharp extremity. Then clean those filtered flesh parts which are in the cut, as far as you can with scrutiny.
Then consider the restoration of the whole wound with the cut, and the upper orifice where it consolidates: and a remaining open fistula in the inner part of the anus, and it will be lighter above the weaker.
And when a fistula is suited in this manner: and it is, when you insert the probe into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and edge of the anus: then take the probe of perforated extremity, which is like a needle, that is, preparing the skins, according to this form. And insert into it a thread wrapped from five threads, and tie around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula, until it reaches its concavity.
If therefore it is penetrating on the edge of the anus internally near, then extract the thread from that opening: so that you insert your finger into the anus, and pull out the end of the thread, and bring together the two ends: and tie both, and leave it for one day, or two days: and as much as the thread cuts into the flesh, tie it well, until those fleshes which are between the two ends of the thread are cut, and fall: then cure the wound, until it consolidates, and is healed.
If however the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate by whatever method is prepared for you, unless it is very deep. For you must not make it because of the lacertum, so that you do not cut it.
Then do with it as we have said, until it is healed.
The shape of the spoon for a patient with a fistula is pointed at one end and not pointed at the other, so that it does not cut what is not necessary.
Chapter 81.
On the suturing of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows after the cutting of them, and the treatment of fissures.
There are two kinds of hemorrhoids. Either they are inside the anus, like vessels containing blood, or they are like a mass of grapes. And among them there are small ones and large ones: and blood always flows from them, and there is one, and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
But truly those that are outside the anus are for the most part small in humidity, from which flows a watery discharge or a little blood with constant flow: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of the one that is inside the anus, is to prescribe a poultice to sit on: and it is squeezed, until the anus comes out, and the fibers appear to you. Therefore suspend them with hooks: or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not retained by the hooks, on account of their humidity and softness, then take them with a coarse cloth, or with a cloth dipped in woolen felt, and extract them with your fingers. Then cut them, and powder over them after the cutting certain hot powders, so that they may serve in place of a cautery. Or cauterize them according to what was previously said in the chapter on cauterizing. Then treat them with the rest of the treatment, until they are healed.
What if the anus does not obey evacuation, then introduce a weak enema in which is a small mordication, so that it loosens what is in the anus and it obeys evacuation quickly when the weak one evacuates.
If however the hemorrhoids are external to the anus, then their treatment is easy and simple: and it is that you catch them with your finger, or you catch them with a hook, and you cut them. Then treat them with what we have said, until they are healed.
And he who is averse to cutting with iron, then it is necessary that you administer their suture according to this method. Take an unwound thread, and insert it into the needle. Then draw out the hemorrhoid upwards, and make it penetrate with the needle at its root from the other side: and wind the two ends of the thread on the lower part of the needle, and let them be crosswise: and constrict the hemorrhoid with a strong ligature. Then tie the thread, and withdraw the needle.
Do this with all the hemorrhoids, and let one of them be discharged: nor press itself, so that it runs out from it an excess of blood.
Then put on the anus a cloth soaked in rose oil, or cerate, and put it on the anus: and order the patient to rest. Then leave it alone, until it falls off.
When the hemorrhoids fall off, treat them with ointments, and the remainder of the treatment, until they are healed.
On the treatment of Fissures. For many times it happens from dryness of the feces, and from constriction of the nature.
When therefore they become old, and medicine does not penetrate into them: then it is necessary to scrape with the points of a spatula, or with your finger, until they become humid, and the outer skin which prevents them from consolidation is removed. Then treat them, until they consolidate according to what is suitable.
If they do not consolidate: then treat them again with a more vigorous rubbing than the first, until they bleed much, and then treat them, until they are healed.
On the treatment of inverse and non-inverse piles, and of anal fistulas, and of boils.
Chapter 82.
Know that Almirmar is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs in the whole body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and toes: and pain happens from them when walking.
It is necessary therefore that what is around the nail be cut, and that it be held with forceps, or with a hook, and that it be eradicated from its root.
Then treat it, and if you want to cauterize it according to what preceded in its chapter.
From dry Athelil, one is a small, rough, filtred, round eminence on the surface of the body. And they often occur on the hands of children.
And the treatment of it is, that you stretch out the Athelil, and cut it: or tie it with a silk thread: or with a needle, until it falls. And if you want, cauterize it according to what was previously said with fire, or with sharp medicine: and now both inverse and non-inverse Athelil are eradicated with an instrument that I will describe.
A boil is also a small, filtred, thick eminence on the surface of the body, going deep into the flesh: and when it encounters cold, it feels like the biting of a ant, and it occurs in the whole body: and most often it occurs on the hands.
And the treatment of it is, that you take a small tube from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather: and put that tube on the boil, until the circle of the tube holds in the parts of it. Then turn your hand with the cannula, until you reach what is in the vicinity of the anthill; and you will put it in the depth of the flesh, and you will eradicate the anthill from its root.
And if you need to, do that with a bronze or iron cannula, according to this form.
Let the upper part of the cannula be drawn to the underside, so that a covering is produced, in order that the grip on the finger may be alleviated and its own rotation.
And if you need to, cauterize the anthill according to what has been previously stated regarding cauterization in the chapter on the cauterizer.
Chapter 83.
Of the forms of instruments which are administered for clysters in diseases of the anus, and of relaxation of the belly, and of colic.
Sometimes the clyster is made of silver, or of gold, or of forged copper, or of hammered metal.
And sometimes they are made small and large from these instruments, according to those in which they are administered.
Therefore, that which is administered for the treatment of little children should be little; and those whose anuses are weak or painful, thus also their clysters.
A large clyster.
The cannula of it, that is, the upper head in which the thread is tied, should be spacious according to this method: and it should have a distinction so that the thread may be tied as you see, and its lower extremity which is inserted into the anus, should be rounded, that is, not open, gentle, strong, drawn to subtlety: and on one of its sides there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the threads, and a little thicker, and there should be a thread in which medicines are placed from the intestine of an animal: or from paper, which is according to the form of a small asafoetida: whose root is one palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes as the revolver suggests, and let there be a space which is between every hole the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a strong thread made from crude thread, which is of ten threads or about that, and apply to it the ureter like a sponge. When therefore the ureter is placed in it, let it be tied at the head with strong constrictions between two distinguishing ligatures. Then tie it up with that.
And this is the form of the circle of the ureter depicted here, and of the holes.
The quality of tying with it, is: that you fill the ureter or bladder with medicine, which is warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the weak person: and beware lest it be very hot or very cold.
Then the weak person should lean on his back, and lift his thighs upwards: and put under him a mattress, that is, a skin on which men lie, or a linen cloth.
Then anoint the extremity of the clyster with oil, or with the white of an egg, or with the mucus of the fenugreek, or similar things. Then insert it into the anus with ease. Then let the assistant take the ureter with both hands together, and express it with vehemence, until he evacuates all that is in the clyster into the intestine.
Then extract the Clyster, and let the weak person lift his thighs to his belly.
Which if the medicine compels it to come out, then let him hold as much as he can. And if he sleeps with it the whole night, it is even more useful for healing.
If however you clyster him for illnesses of the belly, and his excretion is hastened: then repeat the clyster until he is healed.
What if there are hemorrhoids in the anus, or painful apostems, then let there be a subtle and mild suppository from those suppositories with which children are treated.
And this should be the form of a subtle suppository placed on a strictured skin.
Head 83 or Head Eighty-three
I have already spoken in the division on the cure of wounds that which belonged to the book, and I will say here the cure of them with the hand, and with medicines according to the complement.
I say therefore, that wounds are differentiated according to what the wounds are made of, and according to the place where the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are made are often such as a throw of a stone: or a cut of a sword, or a blow with a knife: or a strike with a spear, or a stick, or an arrow: and similar to those from many other things.
Wounds that are made according to the places of the body are such as a wound that falls on the head, or neck, or chest, or belly, or liver: and similar from those members.
And I am telling the cures of certain wounds, so that I may set down this reasoning and rule concerning the remaining wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds: since the discussion of complicated cases will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say therefore. When there is a simple wound on the head and it is not a fracture of bone: consider then if it is from a throw of a stone, or something similar, and has only broken the skin: and it is a large wound, and above an uncertain apostem, and a hot euent: then hasten, and perform bloodletting on the head immediately: and do not delay it: and extract from it blood according to the quantity of its virtue: if there is nothing that prohibits bloodletting, especially if the blood which comes out of the wound is little. And let bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the weak man beware of overeating and wine and coarse foods.
If anything prohibits diminishment, then he will diminish from food and not approach meats nor wine.
And put on the wound if there happens to him a hot aposteme, a plaster made with oil of rose alone, or with wine in which there is astringency.
If you are secure from a hot aposteme, then put on the wound, if it is recent with its own blood, and the air has not yet changed it, a powder which I will describe after a little while: and if the air has already changed it, then put on it certain ointments, until it is healed.
If the wound is large, or is from a cut of a sword and similar, and its lips do not come together with pus, then bring them together with a suture, according to what I will describe for wounds of the belly concerning their suture.
If the wound has already been torn from the bone, and hangs, and there is no retention of it, except in a little suspension, then cut it off. Then treat the wound with medicines, and restore to it hard flesh in place of skin, and order the weak person to be nourished with foods in which there is thickness, such as are heads and cooked wheat, until he is like a pulse: and similar things.
What if you find in the skin a rotting, and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut away the entire rotten part, and cast it away: then treat the area.
If however in these wounds there is an artery or a vein from which blood flows: and it is not stopped by medicines, then apply above the artery. If therefore you find it not cut, then cut it with a spatula, or tie it. What if necessity demands when that which we have said does not suffice, then cauterize it, until the blood is stopped.
If however the wounds are small and simple, then their treatment is easy, light: so that you powder over them this powder: because it consolidates them before it changes their appearance.
Method of the powder for incarnation. Take one part of olibanum and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime: pound the whole thoroughly, and sift: and fill the wound with it, and bind with a good bandage, until it adheres well to it, and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it above with little cloths, and leave it, and do not loosen it while it remains, so that it does not become an aposteme. For the medicine should not be eradicated from it until it is healed.
And when lime alone does that, when olibanum and dragon's blood are not at hand, and also dragon's blood performs the same operation in many great wounds, when it is suitable to be put on them and bound, and they are recent wounds with their own blood, which has not been altered by air.
For if the air has already altered them by some alteration, especially when it is in summer time, then it is not in a position for the intention of this powder: therefore treat it with what we have said, so that you put on them certain digestive ointments: or put on them plasters made from barley flour, made with water and honey, until they emit pus. Then treat the remaining ones with treatment, until they are healed.
If it happens with a wound that there is a fracture of the bone, and it is small, then extract it with a gesture: and I will later speak of the treatment of fractures of the head in what is to come.
Of neck wounds.
If a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference between its treatment and that of a head wound when it is simple.
If the nerve of the neck has already been cut, or an artery: then if it is a nerve, there is no cleverness in it, except that its treatment must be combined with what causes vehement constriction, such as lycium and zegi, and similar things. For they injure the nerves and constrict them.
And do not put anything cold on the wound at all: for the substance of nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most elevated of the membranes: and let that with which it is treated be mild medicines, such as calx lota with sweet water infused several times with oil, or with rose oil and tutia, when it is also washed with sweet water: and other mineral stones, in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then administer a suture: or constrict its lips with powders. Then treat it, until it is healed.
If the wound has depth, or if a sinus occurs in its lower part, in which pus has already collected, then perforate it in the most depressed place in it.
For if an artery has been cut in the wound and a flow of its blood has followed, then separate it, or cut it off, and ligate it: or cauterize it, if necessity demands it.
If the spongy parts of the throat have been cut, or all of it, and the alhaugei have been saved: then bring together the lips of the skin with a suture over the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat, but equal it, and reduce it to its natural figure. Then tighten it with a decent stricture, and diminish it for some days. Then treat it with ointments in which there is astringency and excitation, until it is healed.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then perforate it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them, or as many as you can: and what is not prepared, let it be, until the wound putrefies, and is separated and the protrusion is alleviated.
What if the wound is fresh, then powder over it the powder that I have described. If however a bone is seen in the wound and a fistula forms: then treat it with that which I have mentioned in its own chapter.
On the wound of the shoulder blade.
If it is a thrust of a lance or a dagger: and you see its depth, then consider. If therefore foulness exits from the wound, when it is breathed out from it by the weak, then know that the wound is mortal.
What if the depth is not to it, and it is fresh with its blood: then do not put on it powder from the first hour, nor tighten it, so that the blood is not retained in its depth, and returns to the heart, and kills the weak person: but put on it an attractive ointment, and dress it twice a day.
If indeed the ointment is not present to you, then put on the mouth of the wound old cotton, so that it sucks out what exits from it from its humidities: and make the weak person sleep on the wound, so that what accumulates in it runs.
If indeed the wound has already passed three days, or more, and it does not happen to the weak person a spasm, nor a bad trembling of the heart, nor constriction in breathing, and you see its other dispositions good: then know that the wound is saved. Treatment is thus applied to it with bandages, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
If the healing of the ulcer is excavated and it always opens, then you should know that a fistula has already been formed. Treatment is thus applied to it from its own source or chapter.
And if the wound is from a cut of a sword or a knife, and it is superficial on the chest or back: then treat it with what was previously mentioned concerning stitching, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If however it has already made an impression on the bone, and a fragment of it has cut in: then examine the wound, and hasten to extract those fragments, if they are separated. If indeed they are not separated, then leave them alone, until the wound becomes putrid, for the extraction of them will be alleviated.
The judgment of treatment for other accidental wounds in other limbs, is the same as what we have already said.
On the wounds of the abdomen, and the protrusion of the intestines, and their treatment.
The disruption that occurs to the abdomen is great, moderate, and small.
From a great one, therefore, sometimes the intestine comes out, or the contents of the intestines.
Because their protrusion is more vehement and difficult to treat.
And a small disruption also becomes difficult from another mode. It follows therefore, that their reduction is more difficult, if you do not hasten to push them back into their place immediately: because they become swollen, open, and enlarged: which makes their re-entry difficult.
Because of this therefore, a moderate disruption is better than the others: since with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is difficult in these two types.
Know that the suture of a vein is secondary to four modes.
Two common suture lines come together in the suture of the vein, and in the suture of the other wounds of the body; and two other sutures properly communicate with the remaining wounds. But they are more properly associated with the suture of the vein: and I will describe to you each one with exposition, and declaration.
I say therefore, that when the wound is small, and something comes out of it from the intestine, and it becomes difficult to reduce it: then it is on account of one of the two methods. Either on account of the smallness of the disruption, as we have said: or because there is inflammation in the intestine on account of cold air.
When therefore it is thus, then it is necessary that you warm it, so that you immerse a sponge, or a moist cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water cypress, and cumin, and spike, and chamomile, and apply it to the intestine, until the inflammation is relieved.
And sometimes make a wine in which there is astringency: and it is better than water alone for relieving inflammation.
When therefore you see the inflammation is already relieved, then moisten the intestine with water in which has been decocted marshmallow or mallow. For by that will be alleviated its entrance with something of little importance.
But if the return of it is hurried after this cure, then make an incision in the small disruption, with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first cure is better when prepared, than the incision: and there is no need to cut after necessity and lack of the instrument.
Let one part of it be twisted and acute, and the other part not acute, and the extremity not be subtle with the subtlety of Spatula, but rather more obtuse for a little while: and it is that which resembles a probe, as you see.
When the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes, then it is necessary that there be a reduction of it according to its natural shape in its own place, if possible, over that, because it is better.
When the disruption is wide in the lower part of the belly, then it is necessary that you make the weak one lie on its back, and put its legs higher than its head. And if it is in the upper part of the belly, then put its head and chest higher than its lower parts.
And similarly if there is a disruption in one of the two parts of the belly, then put your intention and your consideration always in this, that the part in which is the wound be higher than the other part.
And so it is necessary, that you administer it in large wounds, and in medium wounds.
In small wounds, put it according to what is prepared for you.
Then make that the attendant between your hands, a careful servant, who holds the whole disruption with his hand, and bring together its lips. Then let him who follows sew from it something after something, and this is the manner of a common suture of one.
And it is that you take a needle, or a number of needles according to the quantity of the wound's width. Then measure from the edge of the disruption a quantity of a finger's breadth, that is, of a doctor's, and insert one needle besides what you put thread in both edges of the skin, with two edges of the suture which is under the skin from the inside, until you make it penetrate from the other side, and now you have brought together two edges of the skin, and two edges of the suture: and they become four rows.
Then tie with double thread around the needle several times on both sides at once, until the two lips of the wound are brought together by a decent union.
Then diminish the thickness of the finger also, and fix another needle in it: afterwards tie it with a thread, as you did with the first needle. Do not cease to do that with what you insert from the needles, until you complete the constriction of the whole wound.
And let the needles be medium between thickness and fineness: for subtle needles easily penetrate the flesh: and thick ones are difficult to enter the skin: because of that it is necessary that they be medium in fineness and thickness.
And it is not suitable that the needle be fixed in two extremes of the skin close together: so that the flesh does not penetrate quickly, and the wound opens before its consolidation, and they do not stretch also with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidation.
